State v. Myles


NO. COA07-118


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


188 N.C. App. 42; 654 S.E.2d 752; 2008 N.C. App. LEXIS 100


September 19, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
January 15, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Stay granted by State v. Myles, 362 N.C. 242, 658 S.E.2d 275, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 108 (2008)
Stay granted by State v. Myles, 362 N.C. 242, 660 S.E.2d 537, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 174 (2008)
Affirmed by State v. Myles, 362 N.C. 344, 661 S.E.2d 732, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 489 (N.C., June 12, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal by defendant from judgment entered 24 October 2006 by Judge J. Marlene Hyatt in Haywood County Superior Court. No. 05 CRS 050808.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the denial of his motion to suppress, defendant pleaded guilty to trafficking in marijuana and reserved his right to appeal the denial of his motion to suppress. The Haywood County Superior Court (North Carolina) sentenced defendant to a minimum of 25 months to a maximum of 30 months in the North Carolina Department of Correction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was riding in a rental vehicle driven by his cousin but rented by defendant. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress because the officer lacked reasonable suspicion to detain defendant after completing a traffic stop, thereby violating is federal and state constitutional rights to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures. The appellate court concluded that defendant was unreasonably detained and thus, defendant's consent to search was involuntary. When the officer asked the driver if he could speak to defendant, they were not free to leave and thus were detained. The officer did not detect alcohol and found no contraband or weapons, but found the cousin's heart to be beating unusually fast when the officer frisked him. The officer also noticed that the rental car was one day overdue, but testified that he did not find anything unusual about that. The cousin's nervousness, in the context of the circumstances, did not rise to the level of reasonable suspicion necessary to justify defendant's further detention, and thus the trial court erred in denying defendant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded to vacate defendant's guilty plea.

Meadows v. Iredell County


NO. COA07-596


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


187 N.C. App. 785; 653 S.E.2d 925; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 2564


November 15, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
December 18, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Meadows v. Iredell County, 362 N.C. 236, 659 S.E.2d 735, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 181 (N.C., Mar. 6, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Iredell County. No. 06 CVS 2813.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed an order entered by the Iredell County Superior Court (North Carolina), which dismissed their claims against defendant counties, alleging that a statute allowing counties to fix their own boundaries was unconstitutional and violations of their due process rights, and seeking class certification, a return of the county line to its 1789 position, and monetary compensation.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court admonished the owners' counsel to include in his brief references to pages in the transcripts, the record on appeal, or exhibits under N.C. R. App. P. 28(b)(5) (2007). The complaint alleged that the resolution was passed in 1992, that the owners purchased the property in 1999, and that the deed book indicated the property was situated in both counties. The complaint alleged facts that would put the owners on notice that the property was located in both counties. Any change in the status of the property was made long before the owners purchased the property. Thus, the owners suffered no injury in fact due to the resolution between defendants fixing the county line, and they lacked standing to invoke the subject matter jurisdiction of the courts. The request for class certification under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1A-1, N.C. R. Civ. P. 23(a) failed as the owners did not own property along the county line in 1992. and could not adequately represent the interests of potential class members who owned such property when the line was redrawn.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Person


NO. COA06-1507


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


187 N.C. App. 512; 653 S.E.2d 560; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 2574


June 6, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
December 18, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Stay granted by State v. Person, 657 S.E.2d 663, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 2 (N.C., 2008)
Stay granted by State v. Person, 362 N.C. 179, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 5 (2008)
Stay granted by State v. Person, 362 N.C. 179, 657 S.E.2d 669, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 38 (2008)
Motion granted by State v. Person, 659 S.E.2d 7, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 164 (N.C., 2008)
Motion granted by State v. Person, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 309 (N.C., Mar. 20, 2008)
Reversed by, in part State v. Person, 362 N.C. 340, 663 S.E.2d 311, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 490 (N.C., June 12, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Mecklenburg County. Nos. 05 CRS 227170-72, 05 CRS 227174-77.



DISPOSITION: Remanded in part; new trial in part; no error in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Mecklenburg County Superior Court (North Carolina) denied defendant's motion to dismiss certain charges. Defendant was convicted and sentenced for, inter alia, first degree rape as the principal, first degree rape by acting in concert with someone else, first degree sexual offense by fellatio, first degree sexual offense by anal intercourse, and first degree sexual offense by digital penetration. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and an accomplice robbed a woman, put her in the trunk of her car, drove to an abandoned house, and raped her while the accomplice threatened her with a gun. Under N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 14-27.2(a)(2)(a) and 14-27.4(a)(2)(a) (2005), the appellate court determined that remand was necessary as to the charges of first degree rape and first degree sexual offense by anal intercourse because (1) defendant sufficiently preserved the denial of his motion to dismiss for appellate review since he was not required to provide specific reasoning to support the motion, (2) his assignment of error was adequate, and (3) the evidence was insufficient to permit a reasonable jury to convict defendant of the first degree offenses for which no acting in concert instruction was given since the record contained no evidence showing his personal use or display of a dangerous weapon. Defendant was entitled to a new trial on the charge of first degree rape by acting in concert with someone else because the jury instruction referred to guilt both as a principle and by acting in concert, which allowed the jury to convict him twice for the same crime, in violation of his double jeopardy rights.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated the judgments for first degree rape as a principal and first degree sexual offense based on anal intercourse, remanded to the trial court with instructions to enter judgment for second degree rape and second degree sexual offense, ordered a new trial as to the charge of first degree rape by acting in concert with someone else, and found no error regarding defendant's remaining convictions and sentences.

 

496 of 825 DOCUMENTS


White v. Tippett


NO. COA07-70


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


187 N.C. App. 285; 652 S.E.2d 728; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 2359


August 28, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
November 20, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Mecklenburg County. No. 06-CVS-2828.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner driver appealed a judgment entered by the Mecklenburg County Superior Court (North Carolina) sustaining the 12-month suspension of her driving privileges by the North Carolina Division of Motor Vehicles, due to her willful refusal to submit to a breathalyzer test.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the driver was not stopped at a checkpoint, and her argument based on the constitutionality of the checkpoint was rejected. The officer had reasonable grounds to believe that the driver had committed an implied consent offense. The officer pursued a person who had evaded a checkpoint and come to a stop in a residential driveway. The officer then approached the stopped car and spoke to the occupants. The combination of the driver's evasion of a checkpoint, the odor of alcohol surrounding the driver, and a brief conversation with the driver gave the officer had reasonable grounds to believe that the driver had committed an implied-consent offense. The driver gave no clear indication that she wanted to call an attorney, and therefore the officer was not required to wait for the full 30 minutes under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 20-16.2(a)(6) (2005), before administering the test. The officer had reasonable grounds that the driver had committed an offense and was not incorrect in administering the breathalyzer test before 30 minutes had expired.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Stay dissolved by Adams Creek Assocs. v. Davis, 362 N.C. 354, 662 S.E.2d 901, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 669 (2008)
Review denied by, Notice of appeal dismissed by, Stay denied by Adams Creek Assocs. v. Davis, 362 N.C. 354, 662 S.E.2d 900, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 680 (2008)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Carteret County. No. 02-CVS-1270.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challengers appealed the orders of the Carteret County Superior Court (North Carolina), which held defendants in contempt of court and denied their motions to disqualify the attorney for plaintiff, a development corporation. Plaintiff had brought suit against defendants to quiet title and obtain damages for trespass.


OVERVIEW: The property at issue consisted of 13 acres of waterfront land. Previous litigation had established title to the property in plaintiff. There was no dispute that defendants continued to occupy the land. The contempt finding was based on defendants' testimony and acknowledgment that they were going to continue to occupy the land despite what the trial court had ordered. The court found that defendants failed to preserve most of their errors on appeal by timely challenging the trial court's orders and the orders in the previous litigation. The court further upheld the trial court's finding of contempt and found no error with regard to the trial court's finding of defendants in civil and criminal contempt. The court noted that defendants were found in civil contempt for failing to comply with the trial court's 2004 order not to trespass any longer, and were found in criminal contempt for their testimony threatening to disobey future orders of the court. Thus, defendants were found in civil and criminal contempt on the basis of different acts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders of the trial court.

State v. Johnson


NO. COA06-1552


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


186 N.C. App. 673; 651 S.E.2d 907; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 2305


June 7, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
November 6, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Guilford County. No. 04 CRS 10068, 04 CRS 98541.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Guilford County Superior Court (North Carolina), which found him guilty of habitual driving while impaired (DWI).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the habitual DWI statute violated the separation of powers between the branches of government and was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority to the executive branch because the district attorney was allowed to exercise discretion in enforcing the law. The appellate court had recently rejected an almost identical argument regarding the Habitual Felon Act. It held that defendant had neither argued nor did any evidence reflect an improper motive by the prosecutor sub judice in the decision regarding the charges upon which defendant was indicted and tried. In addition, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress based on his claim that there was insufficient cause or suspicion to stop his car because defendant's improper tags, standing alone, gave the deputies sufficient cause to stop defendant. Also, the trial court did not err in allowing a deputy to testify as to her opinion that defendant was impaired because there was no dispute that the deputy personally observed defendant and that she based her opinion on those observations.


OUTCOME: The appellate court found no error by the trial court.

Blinson v. State


NO. COA06-1258


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


186 N.C. App. 328; 651 S.E.2d 268; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 2191


April 25, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
October 16, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Blinson v. State, 362 N.C. 355, 661 S.E.2d 240, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 453 (N.C., Apr. 10, 2008)

Review denied by, Notice of appeal dismissed by Blinson v. State, 362 N.C. 355, 661 S.E.2d 240, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 455 (N.C., Apr. 10, 2008)
Appeal dismissed by Blinson v. State, 362 N.C. 355, 661 S.E.2d 241, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 457 (N.C., Apr. 10, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Wake County. No. 05 CVS 8378.
Blinson v. State, 645 S.E.2d 376, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 391 (N.C., 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina) entered a judgment that found plaintiff taxpayers lacked standing under the state constitution's Uniformity of Taxation Clauses and federal constitution's Dormant Commerce Clause, as well as the state constitution's Public Purpose and Executive Emoluments Clauses, after they challenged incentives given to defendant business to locate one of its facilities in defendant county. They appealed.


OVERVIEW: Recognizing that defendant state needed to provide incentives to lure certain types of businesses to the state for its economy to thrive, the General Assembly amended legislation to provide for relevant tax credits. The business received such benefits. The taxpayers sued, inter alia, the business, the county, the state, and defendant city claiming the incentives were unlawful. The trial court found that judicial precedent held that the provision of economic incentives to recruit business to the state involved a proper public purpose, and thus, that the taxpayers lacked standing under the Uniformity of Taxation Clauses, N.C. Const. art. V, § 2(2) and (3), the federal Dormant Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3, the Public Purpose, N.C. Const. art. V, § 2(1),(7), and Exclusive Emoluments, N.C. Const. art. I, § 32 clauses to challenge the incentives. On appeal, the appellate court found the taxpayers lacked standing to challenge the incentives under the taxation and commerce clauses for not being able to show prejudice and had standing but failed to show a public purpose was not involved regarding the Public Purpose and Exclusive Emoluments clauses.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Haislip


NO. COA06-1488


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


186 N.C. App. 275; 651 S.E.2d 243; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 2108


June 6, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
October 2, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Stay granted by State v. Haislip, 361 N.C. 699, 653 S.E.2d 884, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 1067 (2007)
Review granted by, Stay granted by State v. Haislip, 362 N.C. 366, 661 S.E.2d 886, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 343 (2008)
Vacated by, Remanded by State v. Haislip, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 800 (N.C., Oct. 10, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Pitt County. No. 05 CRS 51043.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction by the district court for driving while impaired. Defendant's motion to suppress was denied by the Pitt County Superior Court (North Carolina). A jury convicted defendant of the offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that she had standing to challenge a checkpoint's constitutionality. The appellate court agreed. A reasonable person, at 2:30 a.m., would not feel free to leave upon being approached as defendant was by a uniformed officer whose patrol car's blue lights were activated behind him. Defendant submitted to the officer's show of authority. Defendant was seized for purposes of the Fourth Amendment when she stopped walking toward the apartment in response to the officer's request. The officer stopped defendant pursuant to the checkpoint plan, not in light of the totality of the circumstances. The officer testified that his job as the checkpoint's chase vehicle officer was to conduct investigatory stops of anyone who turned around. He pointed to no specific and articulable facts other than defendant's turn that warranted his stop. He did not stop her because she turned across the center turn lane, because of how she drove down the street, or because of the manner in which she exited her vehicle. He stopped her based on the systematic plan of the checkpoint. Defendant had standing to challenge the constitutionality of the plan by which she was "snared."


OUTCOME: The order denying defendant's motion to suppress was reversed. The judgment entered upon the jury's verdict was reversed. The case was remanded to the trial court for appropriate findings of fact and conclusions of law on the constitutionality of the checkpoint and for entry of an order or judgment consistent with such ruling.

State v. Graham


NO. COA06-837


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


186 N.C. App. 182; 650 S.E.2d 639; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 2110


February 19, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
October 2, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Appeal dismissed by State v. Graham, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 723 (N.C., Aug. 26, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Pasquotank County. Nos. 04CRS052919.



DISPOSITION: NO PREJUDICIAL ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Pasquotank County Superior Court (North Carolina), which convicted defendant of first-degree burglary and assault with a deadly weapon with intent to kill inflicting serious injury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and an accomplice broke into a woman's home and stabbed her son multiple times with a knife, causing him serious injury. Defendant contended on appeal that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to submit the aggravating factors to the jury via a special verdict form and imposing an enhanced sentenced based on an aggravating factor. The court held that the trial court did not violate defendant's constitutional right to a jury trial when it submitted the aggravating factors to the jury by means of a special verdict and that, to the contrary, the trial court was scrupulously protecting defendant's constitutional right to a jury trial, exactly as Blakely required. The court agreed that the trial court erred in allowing the State to reference the testimony of the mother during closing argument and by calling the mother a second victim of the crime since it was victim impact evidence. However, because of the considerable evidence of defendant's guilt, the admission was not prejudicial error. The court also held that defendant was not entitled to a jury instruction on felonious breaking or entering.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

Standley v. Town of Woodfin


NO. COA06-1449


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


186 N.C. App. 134; 650 S.E.2d 618; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 2121


May 23, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
October 2, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by Standley v. Town of Woodfin, 655 S.E.2d 717, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 1217 (N.C., 2007)
Notice of appeal dismissed by Standley v. Town of Woodfin, 362 N.C. 88, 655 S.E.2d 841, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 1325 (2007)
Affirmed by Standley v. Town of Woodfin, 362 N.C. 328, 661 S.E.2d 728, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 496 (N.C., June 12, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Buncombe County. No. 05 CVS 03811.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sex offender appealed a judgment of the Buncombe County Superior Court (North Carolina) granting defendant town's motion for summary judgment in a suit the offender filed challenging Woodfin, N.C., Ordinances § 130.03 (2005).


OVERVIEW: The offender was a registered sex offender, who had suffered a stroke and never travelled without his mother. The ordinance prohibited registered sex offenders from knowingly entering any public park owned and operated by the town. The appellate court held that the ordinance did not violate the offender's right to travel through public spaces under the Due Process Clause. The right to enter parks was not encompassed by either the fundamental right of travel or the right to intrastate travel. The ordinance did not infringe upon the offender's right to intrastate travel as it did not impair his daily functions. The ordinance was rationally related to a legitimate government interest and did not violate the offender's substantive due process rights. The intended purpose of the ordinance was to ensure the peaceful enjoyment of the park system for the town's citizens, and to promote the general welfare and safety of the town. The ordinance was rationally related to a legitimate government interest. The ordinance did not violate the Ex Post Facto Clause as it was not punitive. Finally, the town acted within its delegated police power to enact and enforce the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Moore v. Charlotte-Mecklenburg Bd. of Educ.


NO. COA06-601


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


185 N.C. App. 566; 649 S.E.2d 410; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 1936; 26 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1304


February 7, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
September 4, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Moore v. Charlotte-Mecklenburg Bd. of Educ., 362 N.C. 360, 661 S.E.2d 735, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 418 (N.C., Apr. 10, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Mecklenburg County. No. 05 CVS 11157.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner teacher sought judicial review in the Mecklenburg County Superior Court (North Carolina) of the decision of respondent school board not to renew her contract. The trial court upheld the board's decision, and the teacher sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The school board denied the teacher's request for an evidentiary hearing before that board. The appellate court held N.C. Gen. Stat. § 115C-325(m)(2), stating probationary teachers' rights, did not expressly provide a right to a hearing before the board. The procedure for career teachers in N.C. Gen. Stat. § 115C-325(h)-(j3) only applied to probationary teachers dismissed during the school year. A reasonable construction of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 115C-325(o) was that the board only had to notify the teacher of its decision not to renew her contract once that decision was made, before June 15. Based on the plain language of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 115C-325(m) and (n), it did not entitle the teacher to an evidentiary hearing before the board. N.C. Gen. Stat. § 115C-45 did not entitle the teacher to a hearing before the board because it did not apply to review of a decision of a county board of education. The trial court properly struck exhibits the teacher tried to offer because its review was limited to the record before the board. The record revealed a non-prohibited reason for the teacher's loss of her contract.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Britt v. State


NO. COA06-714


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


185 N.C. App. 610; 649 S.E.2d 402; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 1938


January 24, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
September 4, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by Britt v. State, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 1000 (N.C., Oct. 8, 2007)
Notice of appeal dismissed by Britt v. State, 362 N.C. 86, 655 S.E.2d 836, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 1274 (2007)
Motion granted by Britt v. State, 657 S.E.2d 666, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 33 (N.C., 2008)
Reversed by, Remanded by Britt v. State, 2009 N.C. LEXIS 815 (N.C., Aug. 28, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Wake County. No. 05 CV 012952.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, who had been convicted of felony drug charges, filed an action against defendant State of North Carolina challenging the 2004 version of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-415.1, which expressly prohibited plaintiff's possession of any firearm due to his status as a convicted felon. The State filed a motion for summary judgment. The Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina) granted the State's motion. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff argued that the trial court erred by concluding that the 2004 version of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-415.1 was constitutional because it swept too broadly and was not reasonably related to a legitimate government interest. Plaintiff argued that because he was not convicted of a violent felony and his conviction was so far in the past, over 20 years ago, the statute was unconstitutional. The appellate court disagreed noting that the statutory scheme treated all felons the same and served to protect and preserve the health, safety and welfare of the citizens of North Carolina. The appellate court also concluded that the challenged statute did not violate the Ex Post Facto clauses of the U.S. and North Carolina constitutions because § 14-415.1 was a non-punitive, regulatory scheme. Next, the appellate court concluded that § 14-415.1 did not amount to an unconstitutional Bill of Attainder, as nothing indicated that the statute was enacted as a form of retroactive punishment. Because plaintiff's right to possess firearms was not a vested right, the subject statute did not violate plaintiff's right to due process, equal protection, or to bear arms.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Row v. Row


NO. COA06-1692


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


185 N.C. App. 450; 650 S.E.2d 1; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 1803


June 5, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
August 21, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Row v. Deese, 362 N.C. 238, 659 S.E.2d 741, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 228 (2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Row v. Row, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 6580 (U.S., Oct. 6, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Cumberland County. No. 00 CVD 2694.
Row v. Row, 158 N.C. App. 744, 582 S.E.2d 80, 2003 N.C. App. LEXIS 1313 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, dismissed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father filed a motion to modify child support and to determine the legality of the Child Support Guidelines, N.C. Ann. R. (2002). The District Court, Cumberland County (North Carolina) upheld the guidelines and denied the motion for modification. It had previously found defendant mother to be in contempt and entered a permanent child custody order. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court first dismissed the appeals from the contempt order and from the child custody order as untimely under N.C. R. App. P. 3. Next, the guidelines did not violate the Supremacy Clause. 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 651 - 669b prescribed minimal requirements and encouraged states to act in accordance with them in order to receive federal funding. There was no merit to plaintiff's argument that noncustodial versus custodial parents were a suspect class for purposes of the Equal Protection Clause. As for procedural due process, plaintiff had been given the opportunity to exercise his rights and had in fact done so during a two-day hearing. There was no substantive due process violation. The state had a compelling interest in regulating child support obligations, and through establishing a rebuttable presumption with regard to the guidelines under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 50-13.4(c) (2005), the act was narrowly drawn. Next, based on the financial affidavit plaintiff submitted to the trial court, the court found no error in the findings of fact regarding the children's expenses. Finally, the trial court did not err in deviating only slightly from the guidelines based on the evidence before it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's finding as to the constitutionality of the guidelines and its denial of the motion to modify child support. It dismissed the appeals from the contempt order and the custody order.

State v. Freeman


NO. COA06-1502


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


185 N.C. App. 408; 648 S.E.2d 876; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 1805


June 6, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by State v. Freeman, 655 S.E.2d 716, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 1213 (N.C., 2007)
Appeal dismissed by State v. Freeman, 362 N.C. 178, 657 S.E.2d 663, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 6 (2008)
Writ dismissed by State v. Freeman, 663 S.E.2d 429, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 526 (N.C., 2008)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Freeman v. Jackson, 2009 N.C. LEXIS 21 (N.C., Jan. 29, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Mecklenburg County. Nos. 04 CRS 202076; 04 CRS 074439.



DISPOSITION: No Error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of possession of cocaine and defendant subsequently admitted his habitual felon status. The Mecklenburg Superior Court (North Carolina) sentenced defendant as a prior record level VI offender to 135 months to 171 months imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to dismiss for failure to establish that the crime alleged occurred in the State of North Carolina. Among other things, testimony by a Charlotte-Mecklenburg police officer and forensic chemist provided sufficient circumstantial evidence. The appellate court also concluded that the trial court did not commit plain error in allowing an officer to testify that the substance seized was crack cocaine because, inter alia, the officer had been in contact with crack cocaine between 500 and 1000 times, and the testimony was helpful for a clear understanding of his overall testimony and the facts surrounding defendant's arrest. The officer's testimony that defendant provided fake names and possessed a fictitious identification card was admissible under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 8C-1, N.C. R. Evid. 404(b) (2005), because it was probative of defendant's guilty knowledge and established the chain of circumstances culminating in the arrest. Finally, the appellate court held that an interested witness instruction was not justified and that the jury instructions did not unconstitutionally lower the State's burden of proof.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

511 of 825 DOCUMENTS



Reidy v. Whitehart Ass'n


NO. COA06-1310


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


185 N.C. App. 76; 648 S.E.2d 265; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 1740


June 4, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
August 7, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Reidy v. Whitehart Ass'n, 361 N.C. 696, 652 S.E.2d 651, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 1073 (2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Reidy v. Whitehart Assoc., 128 S. Ct. 1484, 170 L. Ed. 2d 298, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 2250 (U.S., Mar. 3, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Wake County. No. 05 CVS 15227.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs homeowners sued defendant homeowners' association in the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina) for fining the homeowners. The association filed a counterclaim for the fines. The trial court granted the association's motion for summary judgment and a mandatory injunction and denied the homeowners' summary judgment motion. The homeowners appealed and the association cross-appealed from the denial of its request for attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The homeowners said the association was not properly formed. The appellate court held they were estopped from claiming this because they had accepted the association's validity. They said retroactively applying N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 47F-3-102(12) (2005) and 47F-3-107.1 (2005) of the Planned Community Act (Act), N.C. Gen. Stat. ch. 47F, to them violated the contract clause in U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 1, but it did not disturb a vested right, impair a binding contract or create a new obligation, as it only provided another enforcement remedy, and the Act facilitated the parties' intent by solidifying the importance of restrictive covenants. The homeowners' substantive due process rights were not violated because the statutes were rationally related to the Act's legitimate purpose of providing a framework to deal with real estate developments. The association's procedure did not violate the homeowners' procedural due process rights because they had notice, an opportunity to be heard and present evidence, and notice of the decision. The association's cross-appeal was dismissed because it did not file a notice of its cross-appeal with the trial court.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed, and the association's cross-appeal was dismissed.


 

512 of 825 DOCUMENTS



Massey v. Hoffman


NO. COA06-1338


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


184 N.C. App. 731; 647 S.E.2d 457; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 1595


April 26, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
July 17, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review dismissed by Massey v. Hoffman, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 567 (N.C., June 11, 2008)
Appeal dismissed by, Review denied by Massey v. Hoffman, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 561 (N.C., June 11, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Wake County. No. 04 SP 3546.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner granddaughter sued respondent owner, seeking access to the owner's property to restore, maintain, and visit the grave sites of her grandparents, and other relatives, under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 65-75 (2005). The Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina) initially granted the petition. Later, the trial court allowed the owner to amend his answer, and ruled that N.C. Gen. Stat. § 65-75 was unconstitutional. The granddaughter appealed.


OVERVIEW: The granddaughter argued on appeal that the trial court abused its discretion in allowing the owner's motion to amend after the hearing on the merits and erred in granting the owner's untimely motion under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1A-1, N.C. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(6). The appellate court found that it was clear that the trial on the merits had concluded where the trial court announced the ruling granting the relief sought by the granddaughter. Even though the trial court had not entered a written judgment, a judgment had been rendered in favor of the granddaughter and the trial on the merits had concluded. A motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim was not properly asserted after trial. Allowing the motion to amend was an abuse of discretion and caused undue prejudice to the granddaughter. In any event, N.C. Gen. Stat. § 65-74 was a proper exercise of a police power and therefore not subject to the constitutional and fundamental provision that private property was not to be taken for a public use without just compensation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for entry of an order consistent with the oral order rendered by the trial court at the close of the hearing on the merits.


 

513 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Evans


NO. COA06-1283


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


184 N.C. App. 736; 646 S.E.2d 859; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 1600


April 25, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
July 17, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Lenoir County. No. 05 CRS 2889.



DISPOSITION: Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Superior Court, Lenoir County (North Carolina) affirmed a district court finding and ordered that defendant be tried as an adult, defendant pled guilty to second-degree murder and assault with a deadly weapon with intent to kill. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the automatic transfer of his case to the superior court upon a finding of probable cause violated his federal and state constitutional rights to due process and equal protection. However, the appellate court did not reach the merits of defendant's appeal. Defendant's appeal following his guilty plea did not fall within any of the categories of appeal permitted under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-1444 (2005). Moreover, defendant did not petition for a writ of certiorari. Therefore, the appellate court lacked jurisdiction to consider the appeal. Under § 15A-1444, defendant had no right to appeal a transfer decision upon a plea of guilty. N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7B-2603(d) did not establish an exception to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-1444(e).


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

Blankenship v. Bartlett


NO. COA06-1012


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


184 N.C. App. 327; 646 S.E.2d 584; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 1452


March 19, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
July 3, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by Blankenship v. Bartlett, 668 S.E.2d 24, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 813 (N.C., 2008)
Review granted by, Appeal dismissed by Blankenship v. Bartlett, 362 N.C. 508, 668 S.E.2d 24, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 817 (2008)
Motion granted by Blankenship v. Bartlett, 668 S.E.2d 897, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 908 (N.C., 2008)
Motion granted by Blankenship v. Bartlett, 670 S.E.2d 903, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 1069 (N.C., 2008)
Motion granted by Blankenship v. Bartlett, 672 S.E.2d 21, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 1056 (N.C., 2008)
Reversed by, Remanded by Blankenship v. Bartlett, 2009 N.C. LEXIS 743 (N.C., Aug. 28, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Wake County. No. 05 CVS 016827.
Blankenship v. Bartlett, 639 S.E.2d 648, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1315 (N.C., 2006)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff voters sued defendant North Carolina State Board of Elections and Attorney General, alleging that the judicial districting plan for superior court in the county, as established by N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-41 (2004), violated N.C. Const. art. I, § 19. The Superior Court of Wake County (North Carolina) held that the judicial districts were unconstitutional. Defendants appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: On an issue of first impression, the appellate court concluded that the one person, one vote principle of N.C. Const. art. I, § 19, did not apply to judicial elections. The constitutional provision on which N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-41 was based, N.C. Const. art. IV, § 9(1), allowed the legislature to divide the state into a convenient number of superior court judicial districts. The constitutional provisions governing the election of state senators and representatives, N.C. Const. art. II, §§ 3(1) and 5(1), had a population proportionality requirement. The distinction between the provisions evidenced an intent not to require population proportionality in state judicial elections. The trial court erred in not treating a document prepared by an agency official to obtain federal preclearance under the Voting Rights Act as a public record under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 8C-1, N.C. R. Civ. P. 803(8), where it was prepared pursuant to a statutory duty. The legislature's creation of a new judgeship was not arbitrary and capricious where it had consulted with the Administrative Office of the Courts and the new judgeship was based on heavy caseloads and maintaining minority districts.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and vacated.


 

515 of 825 DOCUMENTS



Beaufort County Bd. of Educ. v. Beaufort County Bd. of Comm'rs


NO. COA06-1419


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


184 N.C. App. 110; 645 S.E.2d 857; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 1310; 35 Media L. Rep. 2018


May 23, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
June 19, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Beaufort County. No. 06 CVS 956.



DISPOSITION: Vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Movant television station appealed from an order of the Beaufort County Superior Court (North Carolina), which prohibited the parties and their attorneys from communicating with the media during civil litigation between plaintiff county school board (board) and defendant county board of commissioners (commissioners). The station had filed a motion for right of access under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1-72.1, but the trial court did not decide the motion.


OVERVIEW: The board's complaint alleged that the commissioners deliberately underfunded the public school system in the budget ordinance in retaliation against the board for its refusal to capitulate to funding threats made by various commissioners. The trial court dissolved the gag order after the matter had been submitted to the jury. On appeal, the court found that although the station's claim was moot, it was capable of repetition, yet evading review. The gag order wholly failed to meet any of the standards under the First Amendment or set forth in N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1-72.1. The trial court failed to enter any findings of fact of the existence of a clear threat to the fairness of the trial, that such threat was posed by the actual publicity to be restrained, and that it considered less restrictive alternatives. The trial court erred in orally rendering the gag order and in not entering a written order containing the required findings on the motion prior to proceeding with the trial. However, the gag order prohibited either party or their attorneys from talking to the press; it did not deny the station access to the trial or to court records as provided by N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1-72.1(a).


OUTCOME: The court vacated the gag order.

517 of 825 DOCUMENTS



Carter v. Marion


NO. COA06-863


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


183 N.C. App. 449; 645 S.E.2d 129; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 1089; 26 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 263


March 21, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
June 5, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Appeal dismissed by Carter v. Marion, 362 N.C. 175, 658 S.E.2d 271, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 51 (N.C., Jan. 24, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Surry County. No. 03 CVS 1463.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former deputy clerks sued defendant superior court clerk, alleging that their discharge based on their political affiliation violated the First Amendment, the North Carolina Constitution, and public policy. The Surry County Superior Court (North Carolina) granted the court clerk's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the case. The former deputy clerks appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The summary judgment motion was properly before the trial court where the trial court had ordered a mistrial and thus, the case subsequent to the mistrial was unaffected by the rulings made during the trial, including the trial court's previous denial of the clerk's motion for a directed verdict. The trial court properly granted the clerk summary judgment on the First Amendment claim because political affiliation was an appropriate requirement for deputy clerks of superior court. Deputy clerks served at the pleasure of and were appointed by an elected official, they performed acts on the clerk's behalf, and the clerk was responsible for the acts of the deputies. The deputy clerks also served as the public face of the clerk's office. The appellate court declined to hold that the former deputy clerks had broader rights under the North Carolina Constitution, especially since the legislature had explicitly stated by statute that deputy clerks served at the pleasure of the clerk.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

518 of 825 DOCUMENTS



Richards v. N.C. Tax Review Bd.


NO. COA06-1364


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


183 N.C. App. 485; 645 S.E.2d 196; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 1098


April 26, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
June 5, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Richards v. N.C. Tax Review Bd., 361 N.C. 696, 652 S.E.2d 651, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 1453 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Buncombe County. No. 05 CVS 3665.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After petitioner was convicted of trafficking marijuana by manufacture, possession, and transportation of marijuana, respondent department gave petitioner notice that he owed unauthorized substance excise tax and penalty. Petitioner sought administrative review, and an alternative complaint for declaratory judgment. The Buncombe County Superior Court (North Carolina) granted the department's motion to dismiss. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued that the trial court erred in granting the motion to dismiss. The appellate court disagreed. The general assembly had prescribed two avenues by which a taxpayer may have appealed from an administrative assessment of taxes: N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-267 (2005) and N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-241.1 to -241.4 (2005). Petitioner opted to use N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 105-241.1 to -241.4 to contest the tax assessment at issue. Petitioner argued that, while North Carolina's pre-payment jurisdiction requirements were arguably constitutionally permissible as to those taxpayer individuals who had the ability to pre-pay the taxes at issue, the pre-payment requirements were not constitutionally permissible as to those taxpayer individuals who did not have the ability to pre-pay the taxes at issue. The appellate court found that the powerful presumption of constitutionality of legislation was sufficient to withstand the accusation that the statute was unconstitutional as to taxpayers who were not able to afford to pay their taxes. The prepayment requirement of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-241.3 was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

519 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Borges


NO. COA06-476


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


183 N.C. App. 240; 644 S.E.2d 250; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 1037


December 6, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
May 15, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Borges, 361 N.C. 570, 650 S.E.2d 816, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 919 (2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Borges v. N.C., 128 S. Ct. 941, 169 L. Ed. 2d 776, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 472 (U.S., Jan. 7, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Onslow County. Nos. 04 CRS 60913 - 60919.
State v. Borges, 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 497 (N.C. Ct. App., Mar. 6, 2007)



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Superior Court, Onslow County (North Carolina) of second-degree murder, four counts of assault with a deadly weapon inflicting serious injury, reckless driving to endanger, driving while impaired, and driving the wrong way on a dual lane. After the jury found aggravating factors, defendant received sentences in the aggravated range for the murder and assault charges. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in an auto accident in which one person was killed and four people were seriously injured. The evidence showed that defendant was operating his vehicle under the influence of diethyl ether at the time of the accident. Defendant challenged his sentence and his conviction for second degree murder. On appeal, the court found that (1) defendant's aggravated sentence for second degree murder was proper because the trial court submitted the aggravating factors to the jury by way of a special verdict; (2) defendant was not subjected to an ex post facto law, in violation of U.S. Const. art. 1, § 10 and N.C. Const. art. 1, § 16, for the second degree murder because the trial court had the authority to use a special verdict at the time of defendant's trial; (3) there was no violation of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-1340.16(d) (2002) because the prosecution was required to prove facts for the aggravated sentences for the crimes in addition to the elements of the crimes; and (4) even if the jury instruction was erroneous, it could not have been concluded that the jury would have reached a different result because the evidence against defendant was overwhelming.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

520 of 825 DOCUMENTS



Jones v. City of Durham


NO. COA04-662-2


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


183 N.C. App. 57; 643 S.E.2d 631; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 841


December 8, 2004, Originally Heard in the Court of Appeals  
May 1, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Durham County. No. 02 CVS 02620.
Jones v. City of Durham, 361 N.C. 144, 638 S.E.2d 202, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1329 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff pedestrian sued defendants city and officer, asserting ordinary and gross negligence arising from a accident in which a police car struck the pedestrian. The pedestrian also asserted claims for obstruction of public justice and spoliation of evidence. Earlier, the Supreme Court of North Carolina affirmed the dismissal of the gross negligence claim, and remanded for consideration of the other claims.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied a motion filed by the city and the officer seeking summary judgment on the obstruction of justice claim. The appellate court found that this was proper. The evidence would have allowed a jury to conclude that a camera in the officer's police car had made a videotape recording of the accident, and that the videotape was subsequently misplaced or destroyed. However, the trial court should have granted the summary judgment motion filed by the city and the officer on the pedestrian's claim that the city violated her rights under N.C. Const. art. I, § 19 by their assertion of the defense of governmental immunity to the pedestrian's first two claims. The core of the pedestrian's argument was her allegation that the city had a policy or practice of "waiving" sovereign immunity in some cases but not in others. The pedestrian failed to present evidence raising a genuine issue of material fact on this claim. The uncontradicted record evidence established that claims against the city were never denied on the basis of sovereign immunity, and that claims were paid or denied on the basis of their legal merits.


OUTCOME: The trial court orders relating to the gross negligence claim, dismissing the claim alleging ordinary negligence, and denying the city's and the officer's summary judgment on the claim of obstruction of public justice were affirmed. The trial court's order was reversed to the extent it denied the city's and the officer's motions for summary judgment on the constitutional claims.

Richardson v. Bank of Am., N.A.


NO. COA06-211


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


182 N.C. App. 531; 643 S.E.2d 410; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 809


November 15, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by Richardson v. Bank of Am., 650 S.E.2d 437, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 777 (N.C., 2007)

Motion granted by Richardson v. Bank of Am., 650 S.E.2d 596, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 803 (N.C., 2007)
Motion granted by Richardson v. Bank of Am., 2007 N.C. LEXIS 995 (N.C., Sept. 26, 2007)
Motion granted by Richardson v. Bank of Am., 2007 N.C. LEXIS 1001 (N.C., Oct. 8, 2007)
Motion granted by Richardson v. Bank of Am., 654 S.E.2d 482, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 1110 (N.C., 2007)

Motion granted by Richardson v. Bank of Am., 655 S.E.2d 713, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 1186 (N.C., 2007)
Motion granted by Richardson v. Bank of Am., 659 S.E.2d 740, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 296 (N.C., Mar. 6, 2008)
Review improvidently allowed by Richardson v. Bank of Am., N.A., 362 N.C. 227, 657 S.E.2d 353, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 137 (N.C., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Durham County. No. 02 CVS 02398.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff borrowers filed a class action against defendants, the bank and its subsidiary, in the Superior Court, Durham County (North Carolina), for unfair and deceptive trade practices, unjust enrichment, breach of the duty of good faith and fair dealing, and punitive damages. The court granted summary judgment for the bank on all claims, the subsidiary on loans of 15 years or less, and the borrowers on loans over 15 years. The parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The borrowers alleged violations of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 75-1.1(a) (2005) from the sale by the bank and its subsidiary to the borrowers of single-premium credit insurance (SPCI) in association with mortgage loans. On appeal, the court found that (1) because the North Carolina Department of Insurance authorized the SPCI sold to the borrowers with loans of 15 years or less and N.C. Gen. Stat. § 58-57-35(b) (2005) provided that any gain to a lender from the sale of SPCI was not a violation of any other law, the SPCI sales for the loans of 15 years or less were proper; (2) the bank was not liable for the sales by the subsidiary; (3) the unfair and deceptive trade practices claims accrued at the closing of the loans, and N.C. Gen. Stat. § 75-8 (2005) did not extend the statute of limitations; (4) the sale of unapproved SPCI regarding loans having terms greater than 15 years was an unfair or deceptive act or practice in violation of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 75-1.1(a); (5) by selling an unlawful insurance product with loans greater than 15 years, the subsidiary breached its duty of good faith and fair dealing; and (6) the trial court properly calculated damages under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 75-16 (2005).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

523 of 825 DOCUMENTS



Winebarger v. Peterson


NO. COA 06-734


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


182 N.C. App. 510; 642 S.E.2d 544; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 691


March 6, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
April 3, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Avery County. No. 05 CvS 32



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, dismissed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff executrix sued defendant doctor, alleging that the executrix's decedent died as a result of the doctor's medical malpractice. After the doctor moved for summary judgment, the executrix voluntarily dismissed the action. Later, the executrix re-filed the action. The Superior Court, Avery County (North Carolina), granted summary judgment in favor of the doctor. The executrix appealed.


OVERVIEW: The original complaint contained the required N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1A-1 N.C. R. Civ. P. 9(j) expert certification. However, the executrix later admitted in discovery that she had not consulted with her expert until nearly seven months after the filing of her complaint. Thereafter, the executrix dismissed her action under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1A-1 N.C. R. Civ. P. 41(a) and re-filed the action nearly a year after that dismissal, well beyond two years after the alleged malpractice. The executrix first argued that the trial court erred by granting summary judgment because her voluntary dismissal tolled the statute of limitations even though she admitted in discovery that the expert was consulted after the filing of the original complaint. The appellate court disagreed. Because the executrix admitted that the allegation in the complaint was ineffective to meet the requirements of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1A-1 N.C. R. Civ. P. 9(j), a voluntary dismissal without prejudice, which ordinarily would have allowed for another year for refiling, was unavailable to her in this case. The factual record necessary for a constitutional inquiry as to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1A-1 N.C. R. Civ. P. 9(j) was lacking.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

524 of 825 DOCUMENTS



News & Observer Publ'g Co. v. Easley


NO. COA06-132


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


182 N.C. App. 14; 641 S.E.2d 698; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 490; 35 Media L. Rep. 1731


August 23, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
March 6, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review dismissed by News & Observer Publ'g Co. v. Easley, 361 N.C. 429, 648 S.E.2d 508, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 636 (N.C., June 27, 2007)
Review denied by News & Observer Publ. Co. v. Easley, 361 N.C. 429, 648 S.E.2d 508, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 633 (N.C., June 27, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wake County. No. 05 CVS 8997.
News & Observer Publ'g Co. v. Easley, 632 S.E.2d 177, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 195 (N.C., 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff news organization challenged defendant Governor's decision to withhold certain clemency records requested under the North Carolina Public Records Law, N.C. Gen. Stat. § 131-1 et seq. (2005). The Governor moved to dismiss the complaint under both N.C. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(1) and (6). The Wake County Superior Court, North Carolina, denied the motion under Rule 12(b)(1), but granted the motion under Rule 12(b)(6). Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: Resolving the issues raised in the complaint required the appellate court to exercise its fundamental responsibility to determine N.C. Const. art. III, § 5(6)'s proper meaning concerning the Governor's clemency powers. The case did not raise a political question, but only required a determination as to where to draw the line between the Executive Branch and the General Assembly with respect to clemency, given the separation of powers doctrine. Because the controversy was governed by N.C. Const. art. III, § 5's meaning, the appellate court had the authority to resolve the dispute and thus rejected the challenge to its subject matter jurisdiction. N.C. Const. art. III, § 5(6) carved out a limited area in which the General Assembly could exercise its authority with respect to clemency and required the legislation to specifically relate to the manner of applying for pardons. The Public Records Law did not specifically reference clemency and thus was not permitted to intrude upon the Governor's clemency authority. The news organization, then, was precluded from using the statute to compel the Governor to disclose the requested documents, and so the complaint failed to state a claim.


OUTCOME: The superior court's judgment was affirmed.

526 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bradley


NO. COA06-671


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


181 N.C. App. 557; 640 S.E.2d 432; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 251


January 11, 2007, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
February 6, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Cleveland County. No. 02 CRS 0936.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cleveland County Superior Court (North Carolina) entered a final judgment after a jury found defendant guilty of habitual impaired driving. It then sentenced defendant as a prior offender. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: After a police officer observed defendant driving his vehicle erratically, the officer stopped defendant's vehicle. When defendant stepped out of the vehicle, the officer noticed that defendant had red, glassy eyes and a strong odor of alcohol on his breath. The officer formed the opinion that defendant's mental and physical faculties were impaired by alcohol. After defendant was taken to a police station, defendant's alcohol breath-test resulted in a breath-alcohol concentration of .16. Defendant was then indicted for habitual impaired driving. Following a trial, defendant was found guilty by a jury and was sentenced as a prior offender. On appeal, the appellate court found that the habitual impaired driving offense did not violate defendant's right to be free of double jeopardy since the statute increased the punishment for the offense being prosecuted and did not punish a prior crime a second time. It also found that the jury was properly instructed even though the jury verdict sheet did not specify which of the two definitions of impaired driving applied, as the jury unanimously found defendant guilty of the single offense of impaired driving.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Animal Legal Def. Fund v. Woodley


NO. COA06-358


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


181 N.C. App. 594; 640 S.E.2d 777; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 254


October 19, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Lee County. No. 04 CVD 1248



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lee County Superior Court (North Carolina) entered a judgment that forfeited all of defendant animal owners' rights in their animals possessed by them, ordered removal of the animals from the control of the animal owners, and granted temporary custody of the animals to plaintiff animal welfare agency. The animal owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The animal welfare agency filed a complaint against the animal owners seeking preliminary and permanent injunctions that alleged the animal owners had abused and neglected a large number of dogs, as well as some birds, in their possession. Eventually, following a trial, the trial court entered a permanent injunction and temporary custody order so that the animal welfare agency could take custody and possession of the animals to protect and care for them. On appeal, the appellate court found that the trial court had subject matter jurisdiction to hear the matter since the animal owners could not show that the animal welfare agency was required to have its complaint verified, that the trial court had subject matter jurisdiction over claims brought pursuant to the animal protection statute, N.C. Gen. Stat. § 19A-1 et seq. (2005), and that the animal owners' remaining assignments of error were not argued in their brief and, thus, would not be reviewed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Artis


NO. COA06-443


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


181 N.C. App. 601; 641 S.E.2d 314; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 261


November 2, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
February 6, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Artis, 361 N.C. 430, 648 S.E.2d 846, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 689 (2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Artis v. N.C., 128 S. Ct. 544, 169 L. Ed. 2d 381, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 12038 (U.S., Nov. 5, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Pitt County. Nos. 04 CRS 11921, 04 CRS 11922, 04 CRS 11923.
State v. Artis, 174 N.C. App. 668, 622 S.E.2d 204, 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 2610 (2005)



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Pitt County Superior Court (North Carolina) entered final judgments of conviction after defendant was found guilty of malicious conduct by a prisoner and habitual misdemeanor assault. Eventually, a jury found defendant guilty of being a habitual felon and he was sentenced accordingly. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for malicious conduct by a prisoner, habitual misdemeanor assault, and attaining the status of habitual felon. He was found guilty of malicious conduct by a prisoner and habitual misdemeanor assault. Eventually, he was found guilty by a jury of being a habitual felon. Defendant was then sentenced. On appeal, he contended that his conviction for habitual misdemeanor assault and under the habitual felon statute violated the Fifth Amendment's prohibition against double jeopardy. Specifically, he argued that Apprendi and Blakely eliminated sentence-enhancement statutes, rendering all recidivist statutes substantive crimes with the result, according to defendant, that sentencing for either habitual misdemeanor assault or as a habitual felon violated the Double Jeopardy Clause's prohibition against multiple punishments for the same offense. The appellate court found that his claim had already been considered and rejected. It explained that Apprendi and Blakely applied the Sixth Amendment right to a jury trial to sentence enhancements whereas his double jeopardy claim arose under the Fifth Amendment, which made Apprendi and Blakely inapplicable to his claim.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

529 of 825 DOCUMENTS



ACLU of N.C., Inc. v. State


NO. COA06-62


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


181 N.C. App. 430; 639 S.E.2d 136; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 153


September 18, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
January 16, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wake County. No. 05 CVS 9872.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an organization and an individual, sued defendant State, seeking a declaratory judgment that the term "Holy Scriptures," appearing in N.C. Gen. Stat. § 11-2, referred to the Christian Bible and other religious texts, or, alternatively, a declaratory judgment that the statute was unconstitutional. The Wake County Superior Court dismissed the case for lack of jurisdiction due to a lack of a justiciable controversy. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The sole issue on appeal was whether either plaintiff had presented a justiciable controversy in the complaint. Although it was unnecessary that plaintiffs had an actual right of action against the State to satisfy the jurisdictional requirement of an actual controversy, litigation had to appear unavoidable. Litigation between the individual and the State was unavoidable where her request to swear on the Quran when she appeared as a witness was denied, she chose to affirm to tell the truth, and she then sought a declaratory judgment. Moreover, the State had clearly demonstrated its intent to continue the court of action by its refusal to permit witnesses to swear on any text other than the Christian Bible, and the facts did not suggest any impediment to litigation. There was also no impediment to litigation between the organization and the State where the organization showed that its Jewish members intended to avail themselves of their rights to serve as jurors or witnesses if called and the organization had manifested an intent to litigate the issue by filing suit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.


 

530 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Burgess


NO. COA05-1529


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


181 N.C. App. 27; 639 S.E.2d 68; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 72


October 10, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
January 2, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied State v. Burgess, 2011 N.C. LEXIS 728 (N.C., Aug. 25, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Cabarrus County. Nos. 03 CRS 11234-11237, 03 CRS 52118.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of six counts of first-degree sexual offense of a child under the age of 13 years and the Superior Court, Cabarrus County (North Carolina), sentenced defendant to three consecutive sentences of a minimum of 288 months and a maximum of 355 months in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant relocated to North Carolina with another woman and her children. They lived with the woman's sister and her children. Defendant was unemployed so he stayed home and watched the children. The sister became suspicious of abuse and took her child to the Children's Advocacy Center. The child and the other children stated that defendant abused them. The appellate court found that there was no violation of defendant's right to confrontation because the victims took the stand and were available for cross-examination. Admission of videotape interviews was permissible under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 8C-1, N.C. R. Evid. 803(4) because the challenged statements were made to pediatric nurses at the children's center prior to examination by the doctor. The court properly instructed the jury that the expert testimony was admitted solely for the purpose of corroboration and not as substantive evidence and they could not convict defendant solely on this opinion testimony. It was not error to find the children competent to testify. There was no evidence to support a finding of attempted sexual offense.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

State v. McDougald


NO. COA06-164


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


181 N.C. App. 41; 638 S.E.2d 546; 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 90


October 19, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
January 2, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, in part, Review denied by, in part, Notice of appeal dismissed by State v. McDougald, 361 N.C. 689, 653 S.E.2d 152, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 1038 (2007)
Motion granted by State v. McDougald, 655 S.E.2d 718, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 1242 (N.C., 2007)
Reversed by, in part, Remanded by State v. McDougald, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 136 (N.C., Mar. 7, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Guilford County. Nos. 04 CRS 85405-06.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Guilford County Superior Court, North Carolina, entered judgments convicting defendant of conspiracy to traffic by possessing 100 or more but less than 500 doses of methylenedioxyamphetamine (MDA) and to the sale of a Schedule I substance, MDA. After sentencing, defendant appealed his convictions.


OVERVIEW: Although defendant challenged the trial court's denial of his motion to suppress, the appellate court declined to address the issue due to the numerous violations of its appellate rules and dismissed the assignment of error. Defendant also challenged the trial court's decision allowing a detective to testify concerning his ongoing investigation of defendant prior to his arrest, contending that the testimony should have been excluded under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 8C-1, N.C. R. Evid. 403 (2005). However, defendant failed to properly object to the proffered testimony, and therefore appellate review was for plain error only under N.C. R. App. P. 10(b)(1) and (c)(4) (2006). But because defendant did not specifically and distinctly allege plain error, he was not entitled to plain error review of the issue. Finally, because defendant failed to provide the appellate court a copy of an audiotape played to the jury by the State or the accompanying transcript as required under N.C. R. App. P. 9(d)(2) (2006), the record was insufficient for the appellate court to determine whether the evidence was prejudicial, as defendant contended.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

State v. Desperados, Inc.


NO. COA05-1397


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


180 N.C. App. 378; 638 S.E.2d 4; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 2383


August 15, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
December 5, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Stay granted by State v. Desperados, Inc., 361 N.C. 223, 641 S.E.2d 692, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1379 (2006)
Motion granted by State v. Desperados, Inc., 643 S.E.2d 405, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 183 (N.C., 2007)
Motion granted by State v. Desperados, Inc., 643 S.E.2d 595, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 204 (N.C., 2007)
Stay granted by State v. Desperados, Inc., 361 N.C. 361, 644 S.E.2d 363, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 232 (2007)
Motion granted by State v. Desperados, Inc., 645 S.E.2d 77, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 352 (N.C., 2007)
Motion granted by State v. Desperados, Inc., 645 S.E.2d 381, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 401 (N.C., 2007)
Reversed by, in part, Remanded by State v. Desperados, Inc., 2007 N.C. LEXIS 1098 (N.C., Nov. 9, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Beaufort County. Nos. 03 CRS 651-652, 3929, 4452, 4693, 54596, 04 CRS 44, 657-660, 663-666.



DISPOSITION: Vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Superior Court in Beaufort County (North Carolina) convicted defendants of violating a noise ordinance. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The charges arose from complaints about excessive noise from a club. Defendants argued that the ordinance at issue was overbroad, but the appellate court disagreed. The ordinance was narrow, prohibiting sound amplification only at certain levels and at certain times, and thus the ordinance was not over-broad. Defendants also argued that the ordinance was unconstitutional because it allowed the "the County" to issue special event permits in its discretion with no articulated standards, acting as an arbitrary prior restraint on free speech. The appellate court agreed. Although the ordinance was narrowly drawn, it was constitutionally flawed in that it allowed the county to exercise its discretion to issue a complete exemption in the form of a special events permit, while prescribing no standards for the exercise of that discretion. The paragraph of the ordinance establishing prohibitions and exemptions was an impermissible prior restraint, which violated the First Amendment of the United States Constitution. Because the paragraph of the ordinance under which these defendants were convicted was unconstitutional, it could not have been the basis for their convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated.

State v. Smith


NO. COA06-49


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


180 N.C. App. 86; 636 S.E.2d 267; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 2251


September 21, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
November 7, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Ashe County. Nos. 04CRS050258-050260.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Ashe County Superior Court (North Carolina) found defendant guilty of first-degree sex offense, attempted first-degree sex offense, and taking indecent liberties. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In response to defendant's numerous assignments of error, the appellate court concluded, inter alia, that (1) defendant was found guilty by a unanimous jury where the trial judge was clear in the jury instructions which specific incident corresponded to a particular charge and that the jury must be unanimous in reaching a verdict on each charge; (2) the indictments, couched in the language of the subject statutes, were sufficient; (3) the denial of defendant's motion to dismiss was proper because there was sufficient evidence to support the elements of the offenses charged, including evidence to support the age requirements, that defendant tried to get his hand in the victim's pants, and that defendant engaged in the subject acts for the purpose of arousing or gratifying his sexual desire; (4) despite the fact that defendant indicated that he wanted to speak to an attorney at the beginning of questioning, defendant's statements were admissible because defendant did not stop making statements; and (5) defendant was not entitled to reversal due to the trial court's closure of the courtroom where defense counsel had an opportunity to object but did not.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

534 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Massey


NO. COA05-1636


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


179 N.C. App. 803; 635 S.E.2d 528; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 2141


September 18, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
October 17, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Review denied by State v. Massey, 361 N.C. 224, 643 S.E.2d 15, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 54 (N.C., Jan. 25, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Mecklenburg County. No. 05 CRS 13285.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Mecklenburg County Superior Court (North Carolina) convicted defendant of assault on a female and habitual misdemeanor assault. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Prior to trial, defendant admitted to two prior convictions for misdemeanor assault on a female. After defendant again was found guilty of misdemeanor assault on a female, based on his admission to the prior assaults, he was convicted under the habitual misdemeanor assault statute, N.C. Gen. Stat. 14-33.2 (2005). Defendant argued that the Apprendi line of cases prohibited the use of "sentence enhancers" and that as a result, the crime of habitual misdemeanor assault was barred by the Fifth Amendment's prohibition against double jeopardy. The appellate court held that Apprendi and Blakely applied the Sixth Amendment right to a jury trial to sentence enhancements. Defendant's argument, however, was directed at the Fifth Amendment prohibition against double jeopardy, and accordingly, Apprendi and Blakely were inapposite. Recidivist statutes, or repeat-offender statutes, survived double jeopardy challenges because they increased the severity of the punishment for the crime being prosecuted; they did not punish a previous crime a second time. The appellate court declined to extend the holdings in Apprendi and Blakely to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-33.2 (2005).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Dunn v. State


NO. COA05-1178


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


179 N.C. App. 753; 635 S.E.2d 604; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 2163


April 19, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
October 17, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Review granted by Dunn v. State, 361 N.C. 351, 645 S.E.2d 767, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 423 (2007)
Motion granted by Dunn v. State, 647 S.E.2d 96, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 549 (N.C., 2007)
Motion granted by Dunn v. State, 649 S.E.2d 900, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 698 (N.C., 2007)
Motion granted by Dunn v. State, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 802 (N.C., Aug. 6, 2007)
Motion granted by Dunn v. State, 653 S.E.2d 881, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 1046 (N.C., Oct. 15, 2007)
Stay denied by Dunn v. State, 653 S.E.2d 881, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 1041 (N.C., Oct. 15, 2007)
Review improvidently allowed by Dunn v. State, 362 N.C. 80, 653 S.E.2d 146, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 1221 (N.C., Dec. 7, 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs taxpayers sued defendants, the State of North Carolina and its agencies and officials, in the Forsyth County Superior Court (North Carolina) over imposing a tax on interest from other states' and political subdivisions' obligations, while not taxing such interest on obligations of the State and its political subdivisions. The trial court certified a class and appointed the named plaintiffs as class representatives. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers said the State impermissibly taxed interest on municipal bonds issued by non-North Carolina state and local governments, while not taxing such interest on bonds issued by North Carolina state and local governments. The appellate court held the class certification was an appealable interlocutory order because, if an appeal was not allowed, the State's rights would be adversely affected. All class members met N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-267's (2003) requirement to individually demand a tax refund when named taxpayers made a demand. The purpose of § 105-267 was achieved, as the State had notice of all class members' claims. The named taxpayers could contest the tax for corporations and estates and trusts. Each group contested an adjustment to its taxable income under N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 105-134.6(b)(1)b and 105-134.6(c)(1), alleging the same law was unconstitutional, so the named taxpayers had more than a technical or official interest in the subject matter of the suit affecting corporations or estates and trusts. The certification order had sufficient findings of fact to afford meaningful review under the abuse of discretion standard.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.
