State v. Peterson


NO. COA05-973


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


179 N.C. App. 437; 634 S.E.2d 594; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 1980


April 18, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
September 19, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition denied by State v. Peterson, 361 N.C. 225, 643 S.E.2d 17, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 91 (Jan. 25, 2007)
Motion granted by State v. Peterson, 645 S.E.2d 76, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 351 (N.C., Mar. 27, 2007)
Motion granted by State v. Peterson, 645 S.E.2d 380, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 395 (N.C., Apr. 25, 2007)
Affirmed by State v. Peterson, 361 N.C. 587, 652 S.E.2d 216, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 1101 (Nov. 9, 2007)
Decision reached on appeal by State v. Peterson, 228 N.C. App. 339, 744 S.E.2d 153, 2013 N.C. App. LEXIS 756 (July 16, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Durham County. No. 01 CRS 24821.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Durham County Superior Court (North Carolina) entered consistent with the jury's verdict finding him guilty of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: The victim was defendant's wife. The appeals court found that although a search warrant affidavit did not include any indication, other than the amount of blood, that would suggest a search of defendant's computer would lead to information regarding a potential homicide, and the affidavit only included a wholly conclusory statement that the affiant had probable cause to search the computers in defendant's house, the State met its burden; the evidence and testimony admitted at trial pursuant to the warrant did not prejudice defendant pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. IV in light of other properly admitted evidence. This same evidence was presented through numerous other sources. The admission of evidence pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 8C-1, N.C. R. Evid. 404(b) (2005) regarding an individual close to defendant who seventeen years prior to the wife's death was found dead at the bottom of a set of stairs was proper. Evidence of the individual's death was probative of defendant's intent, knowledge, and the absence of accident in the victim's death, and the trial court found the evidence to be relevant, with seventeen similarities between the individual's death and that of the wife's.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re R.L.C.


NO. COA05-1120


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


179 N.C. App. 311; 635 S.E.2d 1; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 1913


March 22, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
September 5, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Motion granted by In re R.L.C., 637 S.E.2d 545, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1165 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by In re R.L.C., 637 S.E.2d 547, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1173 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by In re R.L.C., 637 S.E.2d 548, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1179 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by In re R.L.C., 639 S.E.2d 449, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1275 (N.C., 2006)
Later proceeding at In re R.L.C., 2007 N.C. LEXIS 754 (N.C., May 3, 2007)
Affirmed by In re R.L.C., 361 N.C. 287, 643 S.E.2d 920, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 417 (2007)



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Alamance County District Court (North Carolina) adjudicated respondent, a juvenile, delinquent for committing two counts of crime against nature, N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-177 (2005). The trial court also entered a juvenile disposition order, placing respondent on six months' of unsupervised probation and ordering that respondent have no contact with his victim. Respondent appealed.


OVERVIEW: The charges arose out of an incident in which respondent's partner age 11 at the time, performed oral sex on respondent who was approximately age 14 at the time. On appeal, respondent argued that N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-177 (2005) was unconstitutional as applied in his case because the legislature could not have intended to criminalize non-procreative consensual relations between minors less than three years apart in age, while failing to criminalize procreative relations between the same minors. The appellate court disagreed. The appellate court rejected respondent's suggestion that it graft age requirements into § 14-177 which the general assembly had not seen fit to enact. Application of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-177 (2005) was permissible when the conduct involved minors, public conduct, prostitution, or non-consensual, coercive conduct. Even if respondent and his partner had been adults, respondent still would have been in violation of the statute. It was undisputed that the conduct occurred in a car parked in a bowling alley parking lot, and was thus public conduct. The statute remained applicable where public conduct was involved.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Kiell v. Kiell


NO. COA05-620


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


179 N.C. App. 396; 633 S.E.2d 827; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 1915


March 22, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
September 5, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by, in part Kiell v. Kiell, 221 N.C. App. 669, 729 S.E.2d 127, 2012 N.C. App. LEXIS 838 (2012)
Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by, in part Kiell v. Kiell, 2015 N.C. App. LEXIS 313 (N.C. Ct. App., Apr. 21, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Catawba County. No. 04 CVD 2494.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wife filed a complaint against defendant husband, seeking a divorce and ancillary relief. The wife's complaint also sought to rescind the parties' prior collaborative agreement. The Catawba County District Court (North Carolina) denied the husband's motion to compel arbitration of the collaborative agreement.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that both the Uniform Arbitration Act, former N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 1-567.1 to 1-567.29 (2001) (repealed 2003), and the Family Law Arbitration Act, N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 50-41 to 50-63 (2005) were unconstitutional as applied to the wife's actions for fraudulent inducement and breach of the collaborative agreement. The appellate court ruled that enforcement of arbitration agreements did not violate the constitutional right to a jury trial. The trial court relied exclusively on the fact that causes of action for fraudulent inducement and breach of contract existed when the 1868 Constitution was adopted. It never addressed if "the remedy sought" was one "respecting property." The wife, on appeal, made no argument that the remedy or relief sought met that requirement. She identified no property right that would have been vindicated if the collaborative agreement was rescinded. Because the fact questions regarding if an enforceable arbitration agreement existed did not relate to the ultimate relief sought, and did not affect the final rights of the parties with respect to their dispute, the wife was not entitled to have those issues resolved by a jury.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

 

540 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Grant


NO. COA05-1295


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


178 N.C. App. 565; 632 S.E.2d 258; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 1637


May 11, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
August 1, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Appeal dismissed by State v. Grant, 361 N.C. 223, 642 S.E.2d 712, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 163 (N.C., Jan. 25, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wake County. No. 04 CRS 010480.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a trial in the Superior Court, Wake County (North Carolina), defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to life in prison without parole. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot the victim, a police officer, with a shotgun. The court held that the evidence about defendant's possession of an assault rifle was relevant, partly to establish that defendant shot the victim because he did not want him to discover that defendant was violating probation by possessing firearms. Thus, admission of the evidence was proper under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 8C-1, N.C. R. Evid. 401 and 403 (2005). The testimony about a pistol was irrelevant because the pistol was not connected to the shooting. The error was harmless under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-1443(a) (2005), however, as there was overwhelming evidence of guilt. Defendant admitted that he shot the victim because he knew he was not supposed to possess guns and did not want to return to jail. Next, evidence admitted under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 8C-1, N.C. R. Evid. 404(b) (2005) was relevant to refute defendant's contention that he shot the victim without premeditation and deliberation and to show the circumstances leading up to the murder. Finally, by asking his probation officer about information in her file, defendant opened the door for the State to elicit hearsay testimony to explain and rebut evidence about the file.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

542 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Crump


NO. COA05-902


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


178 N.C. App. 717; 632 S.E.2d 233; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 1671


March 22, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
August 1, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Appeal dismissed by State v. Crump, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 753 (N.C., June 27, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Forsyth County. Nos 03 CRS 20705, 03 CRS 55896.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Forsyth County Superior Court (North Carolina) for possession of a firearm by a felon. Defendant argued that the indictments charging him with that offense and as attaining the status of a habitual felon unconstitutionally subjected him to double jeopardy by "double-counting" a prior controlled substances conviction and a prior conviction for possession of a firearm by a felon.


OVERVIEW: An officer pulled defendant's car over. The officer arrested defendant and placed him in the rear of the patrol car. When the officer returned to defendant's car, he noticed a handgun in the grass about a foot away from the front passenger door. The appellate court held that by possessing a firearm, defendant committed a fresh violation of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-288.8(c) from his earlier conviction, and his punishment for that new crime could not reasonably be said to re-punish the earlier offense. Rather, it only punished him for the new violation. Accordingly, the mere reliance on the earlier conviction to establish that defendant was a recidivist for sentencing purposes did not implicate double jeopardy concerns. The appellate court therefore rejected defendant's argument that he had been subjected to double jeopardy with respect to his earlier possession of a firearm by a felon conviction. The "double-counting" alleged by defendant in his arguments failed to implicate "double jeopardy" as defendant had not been re-prosecuted or re-punished for either of his earlier convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

543 of 825 DOCUMENTS


DirecTV, Inc. v. State


NO. 05-1250


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


178 N.C. App. 659; 632 S.E.2d 543; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 1651


May 9, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
August 1, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wake County. No. 03 CVS 13324.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, two direct broadcast satellite service companies, appealed the judgment entered in the Superior Court, Wake County (North Carolina), which granted the cross-motion for summary judgment filed by defendants, the State of North Carolina, its Department of Revenue, and its Secretary of Revenue. Plaintiffs had brought suit seeking a refund of nearly $ 30,000,000 in sales taxes paid, pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-164.4(a)(6) (2001).


OVERVIEW: In their complaint, plaintiffs challenged the constitutionality of § 105-164.4(a)(6) on grounds that it violated the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution, denied them equal protection of the laws, and violated the uniform taxation rule of N.C. Const. art. V, § 2. Section 105-164.4(a)(6) imposed a five percent sales tax on satellite companies, but did not impose a sales tax on cable companies. The court held that the tax statute did not violate the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution because when the differential tax treatment of two categories of companies resulted solely from differences between the nature of their businesses, and not from the location of their activities, the tax was not discriminatory. The court clarified the distinction that the differential tax between satellite companies and cable companies resulted solely from differences between the nature of the provision of satellite and cable services, and not from the geographical location of the businesses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

546 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Houston v. Town of Chapel Hill


NO. COA05-1461


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


177 N.C. App. 739; 630 S.E.2d 249; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 1199


May 17, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
June 6, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Houston v. Town of Chapel Hill, 360 N.C. 577, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1497 (2006)
Review denied by Houston v. Town of Chapel Hill, 361 N.C. 166, 639 S.E.2d 449, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1280 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Orange County. No. 04 CVS 2469.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner owner of a home near a closed road challenged an order of the Orange County Superior Court (North Carolina) that affirmed an order of respondent town council that closed the road pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 160A-299 (2005). The superior court granted a motion by third-party respondent university to intervene, found that the owner had standing to present the appeal, and dismissed his appeal.


OVERVIEW: The university filed a request to close part of the road. After three public hearings, the council found that the closing would not be contrary to the public interest and would not deprive anyone owning property in the vicinity of reasonable means of ingress and egress. The owner challenged the order in the superior court. The appellate court affirmed the superior court's order. The superior court properly refused to conduct an evidentiary hearing because under the clear and unambiguous language of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 160A-299(b) (2005), all evidence was to be presented to the council except as to whether the council complied with procedural requirements, and the record evidence supported the council's findings. The owner's assignment of error challenging the denial of his motion to continue did not mention its constitutional basis and was insufficient to preserve the issue for review. N.C. Gen. Stat. § 160A-299 (2005) did not violate the Separation of Powers Clause of the North Carolina Constitution or deprive the owner of a fair hearing because he had an opportunity to test, rebut, and explain the evidence presented to the council at its public hearings on the road closure.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the superior court order.

 

547 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bowden


NO. COA05-635


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


177 N.C. App. 718; 630 S.E.2d 208; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 1218


November 30, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
June 6, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Guilford County. Nos. 03 CRS 74359, 03 CRS 74361.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant for driving while impaired (DWI), habitual DWI under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 20-138.5 (2005), and driving with a revoked license under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 20-28(a) (2005). The Guilford County Superior Court (North Carolina) imposed a consolidated sentence of 24 to 29 months. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying the motion to suppress as the police lacked reasonable and articulable suspicion to stop defendant. The appellate court concluded that the totality of the circumstances justified the officer's pursuing and stopping defendant's vehicle to inquire as to why defendant turned away before the checkpoint. In addition to the fact of defendant's legal turn immediately prior to the checkpoint, the following facts combined to allow the officer to make a reasonable inquiry to determine whether defendant was trying to evade the checkpoint: (1) the late hour; (2) the sudden braking of the truck when defendant crested the hill and could see the checkpoint, to the point that the headlights dipped as the front of the truck drove towards the street; (3) the abruptness of defendant's turn into the nearest apartment parking lot; and (4) defendant's behavior in first backing the truck into one space, pulling out and proceeding towards the parking lot exit, and then re-parking when he spotted the patrol car approaching him. The appellate court further concluded that the superior court had jurisdiction because habitual DWI was a substantive offense.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Formyduval v. Britt


NO. COA05-584


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


177 N.C. App. 654; 630 S.E.2d 192; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 1222


November 30, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
June 6, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by Formyduval v. Britt, 636 S.E.2d 575, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1014 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by Formyduval v. Britt, 641 S.E.2d 804, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 13 (N.C., Jan. 9, 2007)
Motion denied by Formyduval v. Britt, 641 S.E.2d 809, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 28 (N.C., Jan. 25, 2007)
Affirmed by, By an equally divided Court at Formyduval v. Britt, 361 N.C. 215, 639 S.E.2d 443, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 32 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Columbus County. No. 02 CVS 0553.
Formyduval v. Bunn, 138 N.C. App. 381, 530 S.E.2d 96, 2000 N.C. App. LEXIS 622 (2000)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an administratrix and her son, filed a legal malpractice action against defendants, an attorney and his law firm. The Columbus County Superior Court (North Carolina) granted defendants' motion to dismiss. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The legal malpractice claim involved the attorney's actions in a medical malpractice suit in which he had represented plaintiffs. Plaintiffs alleged that he had failed to procure expert witnesses who could testify pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 8C-1, N.C. R. Evid. 702(c). The trial court granted the motion to dismiss on the grounds that in their legal malpractice complaint, plaintiffs had not alleged with specificity that under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1A-1, N.C. R. Civ. P. 9(j), the medical care had been reviewed by a person qualified as an expert witness who was willing to testify to a deviation from the applicable standard of care. The court held that this was error. Rule 9(j) clearly and unambiguously applied only to any complaint alleging medical malpractice by a health care provider. Nothing in Rule 9(j) required any special pleading for a complaint alleging legal malpractice against an attorney. In their legal malpractice case, to establish their "case within a case," plaintiffs were required only to proffer sufficient evidence to the jury tending to show the alleged negligence of the health care provider.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of dismissal. It remanded the case for further proceedings.

550 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Browning


NO. COA05-831


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


177 N.C. App. 487; 629 S.E.2d 299; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 1079


March 22, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
May 16, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Browning, 360 N.C. 578, 635 S.E.2d 902, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 946 (N.C., Aug. 17, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Randolph County. No. 04 CRS 51703.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of statutory rape in violation of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-27.7A(a) and taking indecent liberties with a child in violation of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-202.1. Defendant was acquitted of a charge of crime against nature. The Superior Court, Randolph County (North Carolina) sentenced defendant to a term of 144 months to 182 months in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by denying a requested jury instruction on reasonable mistake of fact as to the victim's age. The appellate court concluded that the requested instruction was improper because statutory rape is a strict liability crime to which mistake of fact is no defense. Defendant next argued that the trial court committed reversible error by allowing a guidance counselor to testify that she believed the victim's account of the rape. The appellate court disagreed, noting that the guidance counselor testified in the context of her role as a guidance counselor who suspected a child had been abused and that the statement was only admitted for the purpose of corroboration. Finally, defendant argued that the trial court committed reversible error by allowing the State to impeach defendant regarding defendant's false statements about an offense which had been the subject of a deferred prosecution. The appellate court found no error, noting that defendant was properly impeached regarding false statement made to police.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Shavitz v. City of High Point


NO. COA05-571


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


177 N.C. App. 465; 630 S.E.2d 4; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 1080


January 11, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
May 16, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Appeal dismissed by Shavitz v. City of High Point, 361 N.C. 430, 648 S.E.2d 845, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 748 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Guilford County. No. 01 CVS 7997.
Shavitz v. City of High Point, 623 S.E.2d 771, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 1466 (N.C., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen filed a lawsuit against appellant city, appellee board of education, and others in the Guilford County Superior Court (North Carolina). The board filed a crossclaim against the city for a declaratory judgment as to the proceeds of red light camera program fines under N.C. Const. art. IX, § 7. The court granted summary judgment to the board and awarded postjudgment interest under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 24-5 (2005). The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 160A-300.1(c) (2005), the city passed an ordinance to enforce N.C. Gen. Stat. § 20-158(b)(2) (2003) (amended) by means of the installation of cameras at street intersections to photograph red light violations by vehicle drivers. The board contended that it was entitled under N.C. Const. art. IX, § 7 to the proceeds derived from the fines that were assessed under the city's red light camera program. On appeal, the court found that (1) N.C. Const. art. IX, § 7 applied to the civil penalties assessed by the city under the city's red light camera ordinance; (2) the superior court did not err by using N.C. Gen. Stat. § 115C-437 (2005) to determine the amount of the clear proceeds earned by the city's red light camera program; and (3) the superior court correctly applied § 115C-437 to determine that the city was to pay 90 percent of the amount collected by its red light camera program to the board. However, the superior court erred by ordering the city to pay postjudgment interest under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 24-5(b) (2005) because the statute was not applicable as the functions in which the city engaged were governmental functions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part as to the state constitutional provision applying to the civil penalties assessed by the city under its red light camera ordinance, the determination of the amount of the clear proceeds earned by the city's red light camera program, and the allocation of funds from the clear proceeds to the board. The judgment was vacated in part as to the award of postjudgment interest.

State v. Hocutt


NO. COA05-473


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


177 N.C. App. 341; 628 S.E.2d 832; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 966


November 2, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
May 2, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by State v. Hocutt, 361 N.C. 174, 641 S.E.2d 4, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1341 (2006)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Summary judgment granted by Hocutt v. Hathaway, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 124477 (E.D.N.C., Feb. 25, 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Hocutt, 763 S.E.2d 339, 2014 N.C. App. LEXIS 787 (N.C. Ct. App., 2014)
Related proceeding at, Dismissed by Hocutt v. Doyle, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 187064 (E.D.N.C., Oct. 29, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Johnston County. No. 03 CRS 54060.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with first-degree murder. A jury convicted defendant of first-degree murder. Following a sentencing hearing, the Superior Court in Johnston County (North Carolina) sentenced defendant to life imprisonment without parole. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court violated the Fourth, Fourteenth, and Sixth Amendments when it permitted defendant's recorded telephone conversations to be used against defendant. The appellate court concluded that the statement was not obtained in violation of defendant's constitutional rights. Defendant was permissibly in jail based on N.C. Gen. Stat. § 122C-303, and there was no Sixth Amendment violation merely because defendant was not afforded the "guiding hand of counsel" prior to the phone call. The appellate court also concluded that there was no evidence that the State deliberately elicited incriminating statements from defendant. Next, the appellate court concluded that because defendant's initial seizure and incarceration were not unconstitutional, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress the evidence seized from defendant's person. The appellate court further concluded that the evidence, including a history of violence and hostility between the parties and testimony from defendant's girlfriend that she thought defendant was going to shoot the victim, was sufficient to support defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Stephenson v. Bartlett


NO. COA05-793


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


177 N.C. App. 239; 628 S.E.2d 442; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 870


February 20, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
April 18, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Stephenson v. Bartlett, 360 N.C. 544, 635 S.E.2d 58, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 785 (2006)
Review dismissed by Stephenson v. Bartlett, 360 N.C. 544, 635 S.E.2d 58, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 786 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wake County. No. 04 CVS 60.
Stephenson v. Bartlett, 358 N.C. 219, 595 S.E.2d 112, 2004 N.C. LEXIS 312 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed a decision of the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina) denying the motion for attorneys' fees and costs they filed after several appeals. The North Carolina Supreme Court denied plaintiffs' motion to allow a direct appeal. Plaintiffs did not, thereafter, file a notice of appeal to the intermediate court.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs requested attorneys' fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988, N.C. Gen. Stat. § 6-19.1 (2005), and the private attorney general doctrine. The intermediate court, sua sponte, raised a defect in the notice of appeal, which designated the state's highest court as "the court to which appeal (was) taken." The error did not deprive the intermediate court of jurisdiction as the intent to appeal to the intermediate court could be fairly inferred from the notice of appeal and the notice achieved the functional equivalent of such an appeal. Defendants were not misled by the mistake and errors in notices of appeal had been overlooked in other cases. Neither N.C. Gen. Stat. § 6-19.1 (2005) nor 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 authorized an award of attorneys' fees. In the absence of statutory authority, attorneys' fees were not allowable as part of court costs. Bailey was distinguished as there was no common fund resulting from the litigation and Bailey involved a class action in which the attorneys' fees borne by the class representatives were shared or equally distributed to the class from the recovery. Plaintiffs sought to shift the burden of attorneys' fees to the State, instead of to a resulting fund.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Pender


NO. COA04-1198


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


176 N.C. App. 688; 627 S.E.2d 343; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 582


May 17, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
March 21, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Washington County. Nos. 94 CRS 1349, 1351, 1353.
State v. Pender, 622 S.E.2d 664, 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 2710 (N.C. Ct. App., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for re-sentencing not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered Alford pleas on two counts of armed robbery and one count of assault with a deadly weapon inflicting serious injury. The Washington County Superior Court (North Carolina) sentenced him to 25 years in prison for each robbery charge and five years for the assault charge. The sentences were ordered to run consecutively for a total sentence of 55 years in prison. Defendant filed an appeal as of right.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by increasing his sentences beyond the prescribed statutory maximum in violation of Blakely. The appellate court held that it did not reach the issue of whether a Blakely violation occurred. Defendant was indicted as of the certification date of the Allen opinion, his appeal was not pending direct review, and his case was final. Defendant did not appeal the trial court's acceptance of the plea agreement, the finding of aggravating and mitigating factors by the trial court, nor his sentence. The appellate court allowed a limited review of only those issues within defendant's appeal of right pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-1444(a1) and (a2). However, it was error to find that $ 1,300.00 and $ 700.00 constituted property of "great monetary value" within the aggravating factor list, pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-1340.16. Therefore, the trial court's finding of the aggravating factor that the offense involved the actual taking of property of great monetary value was not supported by the evidence, and defendant was entitled to a new sentencing hearing. Finally, the victim's medical expenses were properly found to be excessive.


OUTCOME: The portion of the trial court's judgment which found that the amount of money taken constituted great monetary value within the aggravating factor list was reversed and the cause was remanded for resentencing in that respect. The judgment of the trial court was otherwise affirmed.

 

555 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Ripellino v. N.C. Sch. Bds. Ass'n


NO. COA04-1681


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


176 N.C. App. 443; 627 S.E.2d 225; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 537


August 23, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
March 7, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Ripellino v. N.C. Sch. Bds. Ass'n, 360 N.C. 535, 633 S.E.2d 822, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 707 (2006)
Notice of appeal dismissed by, Review granted by Ripellino v. N.C. Sch. Bds. Ass'n, 360 N.C. 535, 633 S.E.2d 823, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 637 (2006)
Motion granted by Ripellino v. Bd. of Educ., 635 S.E.2d 299, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 815 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by Ripellino v. Bd. of Educ., 635 S.E.2d 427, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 839 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by Ripellino v. Bd. of Educ., 635 S.E.2d 427, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 840 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by Ripellino v. Bd. of Educ., 636 S.E.2d 568, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 933 (N.C., 2006)
Affirmed by, in part, By an equally divided Court at, Reversed by, in part, Remanded by, in part, Review improvidently allowed by, in part Ripellino v. N.C. Sch. Bds. Ass'n, 361 N.C. 214, 639 S.E.2d 441, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 34 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Johnston County. No. 01 CVS 609.
Ripellino v. N.C. Sch. Bds. Ass'n, 158 N.C. App. 423, 581 S.E.2d 88, 2003 N.C. App. LEXIS 1184 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an injured party and her parents, sued defendants, the Johnston County Board of Education and others, alleging claims for negligence, medical expenses, declaratory judgment that immunity had been waived, unfair and deceptive trade practices, and under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and the federal state constitutions. The Johnston County Superior Court (North Carolina) granted judgment in favor of defendants on all claims. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The injured party was driving her parents' car when a traffic control gate owned by the Board swung closed, struck the vehicle, and injured her. The Board paid for property damage but refused to pay medical expenses or other compensation. On appeal, plaintiffs argued that the trial court erred by granting defendants' motions for summary judgment regarding the non-constitutional claims. The Board argued that summary judgment was proper because the insurance policy excluded coverage for claims arising out of incidents involving automobiles. The appellate court concluded that summary judgment was not appropriate because the forecast of evidence left no material dispute over the fact that the injuries did not "arise out of" the use of an automobile; the malfunctioning of the gate could have occurred even if the injured party had not been driving a car. As for plaintiffs' claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, the appellate court first concluded that the Board was a "person" within the meaning of § 1983. In addition, judgment on the pleadings was inappropriate since there were issues of material fact as to whether the Board applied a reasonable criteria to its evaluation of the claims.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

556 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Philip Morris USA, Inc. v. Tolson


NO. COA05-340


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


176 N.C. App. 509; 626 S.E.2d 853; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 536


December 6, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
March 7, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Appeal dismissed by Philip Morris USA INC. v. Tolson, 361 N.C. 356, 644 S.E.2d 231, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 304 (N.C., Mar. 8, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wake County. No. 00 CVS 06663.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer filed a refund action, claiming entitlement to the benefits of a "special tax allocation formula" under two North Carolina Tax Review Board orders and a subsequently-enacted corporate tax incentive formula in N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-130.4(i) (1989). The Superior Court, Wake County, North Carolina, granted defendant North Carolina Secretary of Revenue summary judgment with a partial refund to the taxpayer. The taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The augmented North Carolina Tax Review Board entered two orders authorizing the taxpayer, a multi-state corporation, to determine the percentage of its income apportioned to North Carolina by taking the "arithmetical average" of the property, payroll and sales factors. Order 350 modified property and payroll factors for six years; Order 351 indefinitely modified the property factor. Later, the statutory formula for allocating a multi-state corporation's total taxable income was amended by N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-130.4(i) (1989). The taxpayer determined its tax liability by using the amended statutory formula (double-weighting the sales factor and dividing the total of all factors by four) as well as its reduced property factor authorized under Orders 350 and 351. The state department of revenue advised the taxpayer it could not use the 1989 Amendment to calculate its taxes; this suit followed. The appellate court agreed with the trial court that the formula set forth in those Orders was independent from and substituted § 105-130.4(i)'s otherwise applicable statutory allocation formula. And having benefited from the Orders, the taxpayer could not challenge their constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

557 of 825 DOCUMENTS


In re Election Protest of Fletcher


NO. COA05-706


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


175 N.C. App. 755; 625 S.E.2d 564; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 294


January 11, 2006, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
February 7, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wake County. No. 04 CVS 16823.
James v. Bartlett, 359 N.C. 260, 607 S.E.2d 638, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 146 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant candidate challenged a decision from the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina), which abated his election protest.


OVERVIEW: The candidate challenged state election results because ballots in two counties were discarded. He also challenged the counting of provisional ballots by voters who did not reside in the precincts where the ballots were cast. After a certificate of election was issued, the candidate filed an appeal under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 163-182.14. The superior court abated the election protest after 2005 N.C. Sess. Laws 3 was enacted, which provided that election contests for certain offices were heard by the North Carolina General Assembly. Thereafter, the candidate sought review. In dismissing the appeal, the appellate court determined that the controversy was moot. A decision in favor of the candidate would not have permitted him to receive the relief he was seeking. The declaration of the election contained in a certificate of election settled prima facie the right of the person so elected. There was no statutory authority for the North Carolina Board of Elections to revoke the certificate. Alternatively, the appellate court found that the candidate's brief was in violation of N.C. R. App. P. 10(c)(1).


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

558 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Bald Head Island, Ltd. v. Village of Bald Head Island


NO. COA 04-1209


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


175 N.C. App. 543; 624 S.E.2d 406; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 177


April 20, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
January 17, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Brunswick County. No. 02 CVS 756.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff contractors brought a declaratory judgment action against defendant village, challenging the legality of the village's permit fee schedule for the use of internal combustion engine vehicles. The Brunswick County Superior Court (North Carolina) dismissed the contractors' Commerce Clause claim, and later entered summary judgment for the village on the remaining claims. The contractors appealed.


OVERVIEW: The village was an island community. The contractors argued that since the fees collected by the village exceeded the "cost of enforcement" and subsidized the maintenance and building of roads, they were a "tax" because the money raised conferred a public benefit. The appellate court found that, as the fees were based on a vehicle's weight and width, and on the duration of the permit, they were squarely within the legislative grant of power to assess fees based on criteria that bore upon the village's costs. Further, 2002 N.C. Sess. Laws 129, §10.1 explicitly stated that the fees were to have been used to finance "the establishment and maintenance" of the village's roads. Accordingly, the village did not exceed its statutory authority. The contractors failed to specify which constitutional provisions the ordinance allegedly violated. To the extent that the contractors might have been presenting a Commerce Clause argument, the appellate court lacked jurisdiction to review such an argument, as that claim was dismissed pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1A-1, N.C. R. Civ. P. 12(c) and the contractors did not appeal from that order nor assign error to the dismissal of this claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Carillon Assisted Living, L.L.C. v. N.C. HHS


NO. COA05-135


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


175 N.C. App. 265; 623 S.E.2d 629; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 60


October 12, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
January 3, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Carillon Assisted Living, LLC v. N.C. HHS, 360 N.C. 531, 633 S.E.2d 676, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 704 (2006)
Review denied by Carillon Assisted Living, LLC v. N.C. HHS, 360 N.C. 531, 633 S.E.2d 675, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 705 (2006)
Motion granted by Carillon v. N.C. HHS, 635 S.E.2d 295, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 807 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by Carillon v. N.C. HHS, 636 S.E.2d 801, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1045 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by Carillon v. N.C. HHS, 637 S.E.2d 223, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1114 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by Carillon v. N.C. HHS, 637 S.E.2d 541, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1154 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by Carillon v. N.C. HHS, 637 S.E.2d 546, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1168 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by Carillon v. N.C. HHS, 639 S.E.2d 445, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1260 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by Carillon v. N.C. HHS, 641 S.E.2d 6, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1384 (N.C., 2006)
Appeal dismissed by Carillon v. N.C. HHS, 361 N.C. 218, 641 S.E.2d 802, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 7 (2007)
Related proceeding at Ridge Care, Inc. v. N.C. HHS, 2011 N.C. App. LEXIS 1742 (N.C. Ct. App., Aug. 16, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wake County. No. 04 CVS 11191.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applicant appealed the order of the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina) granting the motion of respondent North Carolina Department of Health and Human Services, Adult Care Licensure Section, to dismiss the applicant's constitutional, breach of contract, and damages claims and granting summary judgment for the Department and respondent State of North Carolina on all remaining claims.


OVERVIEW: In 1997, the applicant filed plans with the Department for development of 21 assisted living facilities. Shortly thereafter, the legislature passed a moratorium with regard to assisted living centers. The Department and applicant engaged in litigation to determine whether the applicant's projects were exempt from the moratorium. The Department and the applicant settled, under which the applicant was granted the unconditional right to develop 19 projects. 2001 N.C. Sess. Laws 234 caused the moratorium to expire on December 31, 2001. After that date, all assisted living facilities were to be subject to a certificate of need law. 2001 N.C. Sess. Laws 234 imposed certain financing and construction deadlines on its exempt projects. Contrary to the Department's claims, the applicant's settlement projects were not subject to the 2001 N.C. Sess. Laws 234 deadlines. Under the settlement, the applicant was given the right to develop the settlement projects without obtaining an exemption from the moratorium. The exemptions applied only to the moratorium. The moratorium was inapplicable to the applicant under the settlement. Thus, the applicant was not bound by 2001 N.C. Sess. Laws 234.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed, and the case was remanded for entry of judgment in favor of the applicant as provided in the settlement agreement.

Good Hope Health Sys., L.L.C. v. N.C. HHS


NO. COA05-123

175 N.C. App. 296; 623 S.E.2d 307; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 62


September 14, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]

Motion denied by Good Hope v. NCDHHS, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1245 (N.C., Nov. 16, 2006)
Reversed by, Remanded by, Review improvidently allowed by Good Hope Health Sys., L.L.C. v. N.C. HHS, 637 S.E.2d 517, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1191 (N.C., Nov. 17, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: North Carolina Department of Health and Human Services. No. 03 DHR 1838.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent North Carolina Department of Health and Human Services (DHHS) denied petitioner hospital's (applicant) application for a Certificate of Need (CON) to build a complete replacement hospital in Lillington, rather than Erwin, North Carolina. The applicant and petitioner town appealed. The DHHS and respondent, a second hospital, moved to dismiss based upon the 2003 CON application being mooted by the applicant's 2005 CON application.


OVERVIEW: The 2005 CON application was based upon the North Carolina Governor's amendment of the 2005 State Medical Facilities Plan (SFMP). The amendment stated that there was a need for a new hospital in Harnett County, North Carolina, for a hospital with no more than 50 acute care beds and three operating rooms. The 2005 CON application was for a new hospital containing 46 acute care beds and three operating rooms. The 2005 CON application was in essence a resubmission of the 2003 CON application with some changes. Some of those changes were terming the application to be for a new hospital rather than a replacement hospital, but the plans were for the exact same hospital. Because the DHHS had to comply with the SFMP, it could not have granted both the 2003 CON application and the 2005 application as the number of beds and operating rooms would have exceeded the SFMP's maximums. That would have created a duplication of facilities. One of the goals of the SFMP under N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 131E-175, 131E-183(a)(1) was to avoid the duplication of facilities.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the 2005 CON application afforded the applicant an adequate remedy for denial of the 2003 CON application and made the denial of, and the appeal of the denial of, the 2003 CON application a moot issue. The court granted the motion to dismiss and dismissed the applicant's and the town's petition.

Good Hope Hosp., Inc. v. N.C. HHS


NO. COA05-183


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


175 N.C. App. 309; 623 S.E.2d 315; 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 63


September 14, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
January 3, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by Good Hope v. N.C. HHS, 629 S.E.2d 612, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 579 (N.C., 2006)
Review denied by, Writ of certiorari denied Good Hope Hosp., Inc. v. N.C. HHS, Div. of Facility Servs., 360 N.C. 480, 632 S.E.2d 172, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 391 (2006)
Motion denied by Good Hope Hosp., Inc. v. N.C. HHS, 360 N.C. 480, 632 S.E.2d 172, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 352 (2006)
Motion granted by Good Hope v. N.C. HHS, 633 S.E.2d 99, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 194 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by Good Hope v. NCDHHS, 635 S.E.2d 287, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 668 (N.C., July 5, 2006)
Motion granted by Good Hope v. NCDHHS, 635 S.E.2d 290, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 676 (N.C., July 11, 2006)
Motion granted by Good Hope v. NCDHHS, 635 S.E.2d 296, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 804 (N.C., July 25, 2006)
Motion granted by Good Hope v. NCDHHS, 635 S.E.2d 299, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 814 (N.C., July 31, 2006)
Motion granted by Good Hope v. NCDHHS, 635 S.E.2d 597, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 897 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by Good Hope v. NCDHHS, 635 S.E.2d 597, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 911 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by Good Hope v. NCDHHS, 635 S.E.2d 597, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 918 (N.C., 2006)
Motion denied by Good Hope v. NCDHHS, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1254 (N.C., Nov. 16, 2006)
Affirmed by Good Hope Hosp., Inc. v. N.C. HHS, 636 S.E.2d 564, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1189 (N.C., Nov. 17, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] North Carolina Department of Health and Human Services. No. 04 DHR 0042.
Good Hope Health Sys., L.L.C. v. N.C. HHS, 175 N.C. App. 296, 623 S.E.2d 307, 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 62 (N.C. Ct. App., 2006)
Good Hope Hosp., Inc. v. N.C. HHS, 174 N.C. App. 266, 620 S.E.2d 873, 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 2399 (2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent North Carolina Department of Health and Human Services (DHHS) refused to exempt petitioner hospital from the process of applying for a Certificate Of Need (CON) under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 131E-184 to build a complete replacement hospital in the place of an existing hospital which it proposed to acquire. The DHHS granted a summary judgment against the hospital. The hospital requested review.


OVERVIEW: A CON was required before an entity could develop a "new institutional health service" as defined in N.C. Gen. Stat. § 131E-176(16). Any part of the project which did not fit within an exempt purpose under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 131E-184 remained subject to the statutory prerequisite of CON review and approval, N.C. Gen. Stat. § 131E-184(b). There was only one provision in the certificate of need exemption statute, N.C. Gen. Stat. § 131E-184(a)(5), that allowed the replacement of an entire facility and then only to replace or repair facilities destroyed or damaged by accident or natural disaster. That interpretation adhered to the purpose of the CON law, to control the cost, utilization, and distribution of health services and to assure that the less costly and more effective alternatives were made available, N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 131E-175(1)-(7), 131E-181(a)(4). The hospital was not exempt from the CON process.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the DHHS's summary judgment and determination.

State v. Pender


NO. COA04-1198


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


622 S.E.2d 664; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 2710


May 17, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
December 20, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Opinion withdrawn by State v. Pender, 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 123 (N.C. Ct. App., Jan. 9, 2006)
Substituted opinion at State v. Pender, 627 S.E.2d 343, 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 582 (N.C. Ct. App., Mar. 21, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Washington County. Nos. 94 CRS 1349, 1351, 1353.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; Reversed in part; and Remanded for Re-sentencing not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered Alford pleas to armed robbery and assault with a deadly weapon inflicting serious injury and was sentenced to consecutive sentences totaling 55 years of imprisonment. Defendant's petition for the review of judgments entered by the Washington County Superior Court (North Carolina) was allowed, but was limited to those issues within defendant's appeal of right. The State's motion to amend the record on appeal was allowed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that defendant failed to preserve his claim of an error in the consideration at sentencing of evidence from co-defendant's trial. The appellate court held that defendant did not have to object to preserve his claim. Defendant's Blakely claim was not reached as defendant was indicted before the certification date of the State v. Allen opinion, his appeal was not pending direct review, and his case was final. Defendant was entitled to a new sentencing hearing as to his armed robbery conviction as the taking of $ 1,300 and $ 700 from his victims did not support the finding of the taking of great monetary value as an aggravating factor. Defendant was not entitled to a new sentencing hearing on his assault with a deadly weapon inflicting serious injury conviction as the victim's medical bills after being shot totalled $ 29,837.29, were "excessive," and surpassed those normally incurred from such an assault. Defendant stipulated to the amount of the medical bills as he did not object to the State's recitation of the figure nor take exception to the amount when it was offered as support for a finding the non-statutory aggravating factor of great monetary loss.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed as to the armed robbery sentences and the matter was remanded to the sentencing court for re-sentencing consistent with the opinion. In all other respects, the judgment was affirmed.

 

563 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Barksdale v. Duke Univ. Med. Ctr.


NO. COA05-101


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


175 N.C. App. 102; 623 S.E.2d 51; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 2753


September 21, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
December 20, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Durham County. No. 03 CVS 05753.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff decedent's estate re-filed a medical malpractice suit against defendants, the hospital defendants, the medical practice defendants, and a doctor, after a first suit was voluntarily dismissed. The hospital defendants' motion to dismiss was granted by the Durham County Superior Court (North Carolina). The medical practice defendants' and a doctor's motions to dismiss were also granted. The estate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The estate argued that its re-filed complaint related back to the original complaint for statute of limitations purposes. The appellate court held that the suit was properly dismissed. The original complaint did not contain a N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1A-1, N.C. R. Civ. P. 9(j) (2004) certification. The re-filed complaint was filed after the statute of limitations expired and the 120-day extension, if it had been sought, would have expired. There was no expert review prior to the commencement of the original action, which was contrary to the North Carolina legislature's intent in enacting Rule 9(j). The estate's claim that when the original action was filed, it did not have to comply with Rule 9(j) was rejected. The North Carolina Supreme Court vacated the intermediate court's Anderson ruling to the extent that it concluded that Rule 9(j) was unconstitutional before the estate voluntarily dismissed its original action. After the North Carolina Supreme Court's decision was released, the estate had to comply with Rule 9(j). The estate could have amended its complaint to include the Rule 9(j) certification and had the amendment relate back to the original filing date, but it did not do so.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

564 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Oglesby


NO. COA04-1534


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


174 N.C. App. 658; 622 S.E.2d 152; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 2624


August 23, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
December 6, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Stay granted by State v. Oglesby, 360 N.C. 294, 627 S.E.2d 215, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 1305 (2005)
Review granted by, Stay granted by State v. Oglesby, 361 N.C. 177, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1355 (2006)
Review granted by, Stay granted by State v. Oglesby, 640 S.E.2d 392, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1369 (N.C., 2006)
Review granted by State v. Oglesby, 361 N.C. 177, 640 S.E.2d 391, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1356 (2006)
Motion granted by State v. Oglesby, 643 S.E.2d 593, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 200 (N.C., 2007)
Affirmed in part and vacated in part by, Remanded by, Review improvidently allowed by, in part State v. Oglesby, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 812 (N.C., Aug. 24, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Forsyth County. Nos. 02 CRS 60325, 60329.



DISPOSITION: No error in part; remanded in part for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Forsyth County Superior Court (North Carolina) convicted appellant juvenile of felony murder, first-degree kidnapping, and attempted robbery with a dangerous weapon, after it denied suppression of the juvenile's statements made after his request to call his aunt during the custodial interrogation. The juvenile appealed.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile challenged his convictions. The appeals court first held that because his aunt was neither a parent nor one of the of the listed parties in N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7B-2101, he had no right to her presence during police questioning. Second, the juvenile was properly shackled out of concern of him wanting to run, especially where the shackles could not be seen and there was no evidence that the jury was even affected by, or even aware of, the restraints. Third, the juvenile conceded that his argument as to the murder indictment should have been dismissed where it unconstitutionally failed to allege all of the elements of first-degree murder had been previously rejected. Fourth, regarding two counts of robbery with a dangerous weapon, the trial court erred in finding an aggravating factor and sentencing the juvenile within the aggravated range, since the aggravating factor was neither a prior conviction nor admitted by the juvenile. Finally, it was reversible error to impose sentences for the first-degree kidnapping and attempted robbery with a dangerous weapon offenses, both of which the jury was instructed could serve as underlying felonies to the felony murder.


OUTCOME: The suppression order was affirmed, but the matter was remanded to arrest judgment on the first-degree kidnapping or the attempted robbery offenses as the underlying felony with respect to the juvenile's felony murder conviction in such a manner that would not subject him to a greater punishment.

566 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Helsius v. Robertson


NO. COA05-08


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


174 N.C. App. 507; 621 S.E.2d 263; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 2469


September 14, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
November 15, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by, Appeal dismissed by, Review denied by Helsius v. Robertson, 360 N.C. 363, 629 S.E.2d 851, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 169 (N.C., Mar. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Durham County. No. 04 SP 533.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee deputy sheriff applied to the Durham County Superior Court (North Carolina) for a determination, under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 97-10.2(j) (2004), of the amount of appellant county's subrogation lien and to distribute a settlement amount. The court denied the county's motions to dismiss based on sovereign immunity and violation of rights under the North Carolina Constitution, and extinguished the county's subrogation lien. The county appealed.


OVERVIEW: The deputy sheriff's motorcycle was struck by a vehicle while he was escorting a funeral procession. After the deputy sheriff settled his claims against the driver of the vehicle for the limits of her liability insurance, he received an insurance payment as a result of underinsured motorists coverage. The county paid the deputy sheriff workers' compensation benefits for medical expenses, temporary total disability, and permanent partial disability compensation. On appeal, the court found that, based upon the fact that the county government was subject to the North Carolina Workers' Compensation Act and its provisions regarding payment and compensation under the Act, there was specific statutory authority authorizing the deputy sheriff to seek a determination under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 97-10.2(j) of the county's authority to file a lien against his settlement proceeds. Further, N.C. Gen. Stat. § 97-10.2(j) did not violate the Exclusive Emoluments Clause of N.C. Const. art. I, § 32. Finally, the trial court's extinguishment of the lien under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 97-10.2(j) was supported by sufficient findings of fact and conclusions of law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. McMahan


NO. COA05-211


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


174 N.C. App. 586; 621 S.E.2d 319; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 2477


October 19, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
November 15, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Stay granted by State v. McMahan, 360 N.C. 179, 625 S.E.2d 550, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 1272 (2005)
Review granted by, Stay granted by State v. McMahan, 361 N.C. 176, 640 S.E.2d 390, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1372 (2006)
Reversed by State v. McMahan, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 589 (N.C., June 28, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Vacated and Remanded for New Sentencing Hearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cabarrus County Superior Court (North Carolina) revoked defendant's probation term and activated her suspended sentences. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue on appeal was whether the trial court erred by activating defendant's suspended sentences where those sentences were unconstitutionally aggravated in violation of Blakely v. Washington. The State alleged that this issue was not preserved for review as defendant failed to object to the imposing an aggravated sentence upon the revocation of her probation. However, N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-1446(d)(18) (2003) permitted review of sentencing errors even though defendant failed to object at trial. Second, the amended record failed to indicate that defendant stipulated to the relevant facts or consented to judicial fact finding of aggravating factors. Third, the court took judicial notice of the plea transcript and the trial court's findings of aggravation and mitigation and amended the record to include these documents ex mero moto. Defendant then argued that the trial court erred in activating her suspended sentences where those sentences were unconstitutionally aggravated without her stipulation or submission of the aggravating factors to a jury to be proven beyond a reasonable doubt. The appeals court agreed, warranting remand for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was vacated, and the matter was remanded for a new sentencing hearing.

N.C. Bd. of Pharm. v. Rules Review Comm'n


NO. COA04-929


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


174 N.C. App. 301; 620 S.E.2d 893; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 2362


April 19, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
November 1, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by NC Bd. of Pharm. v. Comm'n, 627 S.E.2d 466, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1479 (N.C., 2006)
Review granted by, Appeal dismissed by N.C. Bd. of Pharm. v. Rules Review Comm'n, 360 N.C. 483, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 252 (2006)
Motion granted by NC Bd. of Pharm. v. Comm'n, 632 S.E.2d 168, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 224 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by NC Bd. of Pharm. v. Rules Review Comm'n, 633 S.E.2d 95, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 375 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by NC Bd. of Pharm. v. Comm'n, 633 S.E.2d 97, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 368 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by NC Bd. of Pharm. v. Rules Review Comm'n, 633 S.E.2d 96, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 350 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by NC Bd. of Pharm. v. Rules Review Comm'n, 633 S.E.2d 96, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 217 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by NC Bd. of Pharm. v. Comm'n, 633 S.E.2d 100, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 386 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by NC Bd. of Pharm. v. Comm'n, 633 S.E.2d 463, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 196 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by NC Bd. of Pharm. v. Comm'n, 633 S.E.2d 469, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 513 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by NC Bd. of Pharm. v. Comm'n, 635 S.E.2d 297, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 805 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by NC Bd. of Pharm. v. Comm'n, 635 S.E.2d 425, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 825 (N.C., 2006)
Reversed by, in part, Remanded by, Review improvidently allowed by N.C. Bd. of Pharm. v. Rules Review Comm'n, 360 N.C. 638, 637 S.E.2d 515, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1188 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wake County. No. 99 CVS 06558.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff board sued defendant commission, seeking a declaratory judgment that the commission's actions in refusing to validate a proposed rule were unconstitutional and that the board had statutory authority to enact the proposed rule. The board also sought injunctive relief. The Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina) found in favor of the commission. The board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The rule at issue addressed pharmacist working hours. The appellate court held that the board's authority to regulate pharmacies did not extend to regulating working hours as set out in proposed rule. The North Carolina Department of Labor was the only entity with authority to regulate working hours of pharmacists in pharmacies. Contrary to the board's argument, none of the statutes cited by it, N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 90-85.6(a), 90-85.21(a), 90-85.32, provided authority for the board to enact the proposed rule. By proposing the rule, the board sought the benefit of the commission's approval. However, the board did not challenge the constitutionality of the rule-making process until the commission objected to the proposed rule. Only after the board received an unfavorable outcome did it allege the process was unconstitutional. Thus, the board was estopped from raising a constitutional challenge to the commission's authority, and the trial court did not err by refusing to rule on that challenge.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Good Hope Hosp., Inc. v. N.C. HHS, Div. of Facility Servs.


NO. COA04-1008


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


174 N.C. App. 266; 620 S.E.2d 873; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 2399


March 23, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
November 1, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Good Hope Hosp., Inc. v. N.C. HHS, 175 N.C. App. 309, 623 S.E.2d 315, 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 63 (N.C. Ct. App., Jan. 3, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Harnett County. No. 04 CVS 145.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital joint venture sued appellees, the North Carolina Department of Health and Human Services and the regional hospital, in the Harnett County Superior Court (North Carolina), to permit the construction of a new hospital under the exemption provisions of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 131E-184(a). Appellant town intervened as a plaintiff. The trial court found for the Department and the regional hospital. The joint venture and the town appealed.


OVERVIEW: The hospital joint venture, which was denied a certificate of need to build a new hospital by the Department after the regional hospital commented against the proposed new hospital, contended that it could develop a replacement hospital without the issuance of a certificate of need. On appeal, the court found that (1) the trial court properly dismissed the constitutional claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and the request for declaratory judgment because the hospital joint venture and the town failed to exhaust their administrative remedies by pursuing an administrative review hearing pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 131E-78(b)(1); (2) the claim for injunctive relief was properly dismissed because the available administrative remedies were not inadequate; (3) the equal protection claim under N.C. Const. art. I, § 19 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV was properly dismissed because it failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted in that it failed to allege the lack of a rational basis; and (4) the claims against the regional hospital were properly dismissed because the complaint failed to meet the heightened standard required to overcome the regional hospital's Noerr immunity.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Fabrikant v. Currituck County


NO. COA04-250


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


174 N.C. App. 30; 621 S.E.2d 19; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 2219


October 20, 2004, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
October 18, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Currituck County. No. 98 CVS 153.
Fabrikant v. Currituck County, 597 S.E.2d 129, 2004 N.C. LEXIS 537 (N.C., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed the orders of the Currituck County Superior Court (North Carolina), which dismissed their claims against defendants, the State of North Carolina, the State of North Carolina Department of Environment and Natural Resources, the Coastal Resources Commission, the Division of Coastal Management, and its director. Plaintiffs sought a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sought a declaratory judgment that they had exclusive ownership of the portion of a beach between the high tide mark and the vegetation line, identified as the dry sand beach. Plaintiffs sought to quiet title in that portion of the beach and, to that end, requested injunctive relief. Plaintiffs asserted that their developer had owned the portion of the beach at issue and had deeded the same to each plaintiff in their respective deeds. Plaintiffs' suit arose from various alleged negative conduct resulting from the public's use of the dry sand beach in front of their homes, including litter, noise, bonfires, relief of bodily functions, requests for use of the bathroom and the telephone, and unauthorized use of plaintiffs' outdoor showers. The court held, however, that plaintiffs' causes of action were barred because plaintiffs failed to properly allege in their complaint the State's waiver of sovereign immunity. Plaintiffs' reliance on N.C. Gen. Stat. § 41-10.1 (2003) as to waiver was misplaced since they failed to allege that defendants asserted any claim of title to the beach area.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's orders dismissing plaintiffs' claims against defendants.

Parker v. New Hanover County


NO. COA04-1093


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


173 N.C. App. 644; 619 S.E.2d 868; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 2227


March 24, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
October 18, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] New Hanover County. No. 02 CVS 4738.
Parker v. Figure "8" Beach Homeowners' Ass'n, 170 N.C. App. 145, 611 S.E.2d 874, 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 907 (N.C. Ct. App., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner challenged a decision from the New Hanover County Superior Court (North Carolina), which entered summary judgment in favor of defendant county in a dispute regarding a special assessment. The owner also challenged the denial of his motion for partial summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The owner challenged a special assessment imposed for the relocation of an inlet on the coast. The county's motion for summary judgment was granted, and the owner sought review. In affirming, the court determined that the project did not violate N.C. Const. art. V, § 2, cl. 1 because the special assessment was imposed for a public purpose. Under the applicable two-prong test, the court determined that the assessment involved a reasonable connection with the convenience and necessity of the county. In making this decision, the court looked to the North Carolina Constitution, the public trust, and the public policy of North Carolina. Second, the activity benefitted the public in general since it resulted in a conservation of beaches. Next, the court held that the project complied with N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 153A-185, 153A-186. Although the owner was permitted to challenge the special assessment, he was not allowed to challenge the choice of the methods used. In addition, the inlet project was one for which a special assessment was authorized under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 153A-185. Finally, the owner's constitutional claims were not preserved for appellate review.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Motion granted by State v. Jacobs, 632 S.E.2d 767, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 346 (N.C., 2006)
Review granted by, Stay granted by State v. Jacobs, 361 N.C. 175, 640 S.E.2d 389, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1351 (2006)
Review denied by State v. Jacobs, 361 N.C. 175, 640 S.E.2d 389, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1349 (2006)
Vacated by, in part, Reversed by, in part, Remanded by State v. Jacobs, 361 N.C. 565, 648 S.E.2d 841, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 814 (N.C., Aug. 24, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Robeson County. No. 02 CRS 55299, 02 CRS 55302-05, 02 CRS 55319-20, 02 CRS 55322-24.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the judgment of the Robeson County Court (North Carolina), which convicted defendants for impersonation of a law enforcement officer, robbery with a dangerous weapon, first-degree burglary, and two counts of second-degree kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were alleged to have entered a residence under the auspices of being detectives. Defendants were alleged to have tied up and bound the victims and ransacked the homes, stealing money. Defendants asserted various trial court errors on appeal but the court found no error with regard to any violation of one defendant's right to remain silent as to another similar incident, because the uncontradicted testimony indicated that the law enforcement officials involved in the investigation at bar honored that defendant's invocation of his right to remain silent regarding the second incident. Also, the trial court did not abuse its discretion by admitting evidence of a prior incident because the two were very similar and the trial court judge repeatedly gave the jury a limiting instruction. The court did find error with the trial court failing to submit the aggravating factors to the jury for proof beyond a reasonable doubt and the imposition of attorney's fees against one defendant was in error since that defendant was not given a hearing on the matter.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's imposition of attorney's fees upon one defendant and remanded the case for resentencing.

State v. Cruz


NO. COA04-1217


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


173 N.C. App. 689; 620 S.E.2d 251; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 2288


May 18, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
October 18, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Pitt County. No. 03 CRS 53184.



DISPOSITION: No error in part, reversed in part, remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Pitt County Superior Court (North Carolina) denied defendant's motion to dismiss and entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of driving while impaired and driving while license revoked. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for, inter alia, driving while impaired and driving while license revoked. In his case, he and his nephew had obtained a large amount of beer and consumed it. The nephew then drove off and had a fatal car accident. Defendant drove up to the accident scene and later gave statements to police. The trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the charges. At trial, the State relied on the confessions to prove that defendant drove a car. The State also had several witnesses testify about observing defendant's driving and a police officer testify about defendant's license being revoked. Defendant was convicted of both offenses. The trial court, in sentencing him on the driving while impaired conviction, found a grossly aggravating factor. On appeal, the appellate court found the motion to dismiss was properly denied as to the driving while impaired charge since the confessions were properly corroborated, but was improperly denied as to the driving while license revoked since sufficient "knowledge" evidence was not presented. It also found that the grossly aggravating factor should have been submitted to the jury for it to find beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's conviction for driving while impaired. It reversed defendant's conviction for driving while license revoked. Further, it found defendant was improperly sentenced on the driving while impaired conviction and, thus, that the case had to be remanded to the trial court for a new sentencing hearing on that conviction.

State v. Hall


NO. COA04-1626


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


173 N.C. App. 735; 620 S.E.2d 309; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 2295


August 24, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
October 18, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Appeal dismissed by State v. Hall, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 481 (N.C., Jan. 26, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Caldwell County. No. 01 CRS 52699.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Caldwell County Superior Court (North Carolina) convicted defendant of Misdemeanor Death by Vehicle. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was pulling a trailer with his truck. The trailer was attached to the truck by a hitch, but without safety chains or cables. The trailer came loose from the hitch while defendant was driving, crossed into opposing lanes of travel and struck an oncoming vehicle, killing its driver. The appellate court found that the magistrate's order charging defendant with the offense of misdemeanor death by vehicle clearly provided that the charge was based on defendant's failure to secure the trailer to his vehicle with safety chains or cables as required by N.C. Gen. Stat. § 20-123(b). The order was sufficient to apprise defendant of the charge against him and to allow him to prepare a defense against the charge. N.C. Gen. Stat. § 20-123(c) required the use of safety chains or cables when a ball hitch was the primary towing attachment. Accordingly, a jury instruction regarding locking pins was not a correct statement of the law as it was undisputed that the primary towing attachment used by defendant was a ball hitch. Defendant did not raise his argument that § 20-123 was unconstitutionally vague before the trial court, and thus the appellate court declined to review it.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Highsmith


NO. COA04-1675


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


173 N.C. App. 600; 619 S.E.2d 586; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 2123


August 25, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
October 4, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Craven County. No. 04 CRS 1434.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of driving while impaired and driving left of center. Based on defendant's stipulation, the court found defendant guilty of habitual driving while impaired. The Superior Court in Craven County (North Carolina) consolidated the charges and sentenced defendant to 19 to 23 months in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in allowing his uncorroborated statements into evidence. The appellate court noted that expert testimony about the effects of the drug defendant alleged he took and testimony from the arresting trooper about defendant's behavior corroborated defendant's statement. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss for insufficient evidence as the State failed to present evidence that he knowingly consumed an impairing substance. The appellate court noted that defendant should have been warned that the substance he allegedly consumed could impair him and thus, he was on notice that, by driving after consuming it, he risked crossing over the line into the territory of proscribed conduct. Defendant was not entitled to a jury instruction on involuntary intoxication as he presented no evidence he was forced to take the medication; rather he asserted he took it voluntarily but did not know it was intoxicating. Finally, the appellate court held that defendant was not entitled to a mistrial due to an improper comment during by the prosecutor since the jury received a curative instruction.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.
