Coley v. State


NO. COA04-1141


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


173 N.C. App. 481; 620 S.E.2d 25; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 2104


April 20, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
October 4, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by Coley v. State, 360 N.C. 292, 627 S.E.2d 218, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 1336 (N.C., 2005)
Motion granted by Coley v. State, 630 S.E.2d 456, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 179 (N.C., Mar. 7, 2006)
Modified by Coley v. State, 360 N.C. 493, 631 S.E.2d 121, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 594 (N.C., June 30, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wake County. No. 03 CVS 005581.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers filed a class action suit against defendant State, and others, seeking a declaration that 2001 N.C. Sess. Laws 424 violated N.C. Const. art. I, § 16. The Superior Court, Wake County (North Carolina), denied the taxpayers' motion for summary judgment and granted the State's motion to dismiss. The taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers argued that 2001 N.C. Sess. Laws 424 enacted a tax on wages and other income already earned and, thus, was a retroactive tax in violation of N.C. Const. art. I, § 16. The appellate court found that the plain language of N.C. Const. art. I, § 16 did not indicate in any way that the prohibition on retrospective taxes included a prohibition on a retrospective increase on an income tax rate. This case involved a new tax rate, not an entirely new tax. Moreover, the new tax rate began to apply only in the year in which the statute was enacted. At this point, neither an individual's annual income nor tax liability under the statute had yet been determined. Furthermore, the increased tax rate was not ineffectual in light of any purpose of 2001 N.C. Sess. Laws 424. Because the increase in the income tax rate under 2001 N.C. Sess. Laws 424 was not a tax upon an act, the statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Goldston v. State


NO. COA04-593


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


173 N.C. App. 416; 618 S.E.2d 785; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 2012


June 13, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
September 20, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by Goldston & Harrington v. State, 629 S.E.2d 850, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 134 (N.C., 2006)
Review granted by, in part, Review denied by, in part, Review dismissed by, in part Goldston v. State, 360 N.C. 363, 629 S.E.2d 850, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 157 (2006)
Motion granted by Goldston & Harrington v. State, 630 S.E.2d 671, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 301 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by Goldston & Harrington v. State, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 306 (N.C., Mar. 30, 2006)
Motion granted by Goldston v. State, 632 S.E.2d 170, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 427 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by Goldston v. State, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1029 (N.C., Sept. 26, 2006)
Reversed by, Remanded by Goldston v. State, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1300 (N.C., Dec. 15, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wake County. No. 02 CVS 015253.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens sued governmental defendants, challenging a $ 125 million loan from a highway trust fund (HTF) authorized by the North Carolina General Assembly and an $ 80 million transfer from the HTF authorized by the Governor of North Carolina. The Wake County Superior Court, North Carolina, granted summary judgment in favor of defendants. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs alleged that these withdrawals from the HTF violated the North Carolina Constitution. The court held that plaintiffs did not have standing to pursue their lawsuit. Plaintiffs' complaint did not claim that they suffered injury from the collection of the taxes which benefited the HTF. Rather, it challenged only certain withdrawals of taxpayer money from the HTF, which affected plaintiffs in the same way that it affected all citizens and taxpayers of the state. Thus, plaintiffs lacked standing to bring their action directly as injured taxpayers. Plaintiffs also contended that, as citizens, they had "constitutional standing" to bring this action. However, during the course of the litigation, plaintiffs abnegated their prayer for mandamus. Thus, plaintiffs were no longer seeking to have the allegedly wrongly withdrawn funds replenished, and their remaining requests for relief sought only a judicial declaration that the legislative and executive branches should not have made the challenged withdrawals from the HTF and should not make such withdrawals again. Therefore, plaintiffs' action as citizens was for an advisory declaration, which they had no standing to seek.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Morton


NO. COA04-1484


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 2029


May 19, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals

583 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. McBride


NO. COA03-740


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


173 N.C. App. 101; 618 S.E.2d 754; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 1897


August 24, 2004, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
September 6, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by State v. McBride, 623 S.E.2d 269, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 1105 (N.C., 2005)
Review denied by State v. McBride, 360 N.C. 179, 626 S.E.2d 835, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 1276 (2005)
Appeal dismissed by State v. McBride, 2006 N.C. App. LEXIS 2001 (N.C. Ct. App., Oct. 3, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Richmond County. Nos. 01 CRS 4184, 51293-94.



DISPOSITION: No prejudicial error in part; remanded for clerical changes and resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for possession of drug paraphernalia, possession of cocaine, maintaining a place to keep controlled substances, and being an habitual felon. After a jury trial, defendant was convicted on all charges but that of maintaining a place to keep controlled substances. The Richmond County Superior Court (North Carolina) imposed a sentence in the aggravated range. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Among other things, defendant argued that the trial court erred in admitting evidence that a witness had the reputation for being a user of illegal drugs such as crack cocaine and that defendant's brother had the reputation for being a dealer of drugs. While the appellate court concluded that the admission of the reputation evidence violated N.C. Gen. Stat. § 8C-1, N.C. R. Evid. 404(a), the appellate court found that the error was not prejudicial since the evidence regarding the witness was cumulative and there was ample evidence to convict defendant without evidence of his brother's reputation. The appellate court also held that the denial of defendant's motion to dismiss the possession charges was proper because the State presented sufficient evidence of constructive possession, including evidence that defendant smelled of crack cocaine, had the characteristics of someone under the influence of drugs, and attempted to get inside his motel room when the officer approached. Next, the appellate court concluded that the erroneous entry of judgment and commitment for defendant under the habitual felon case number was merely a clerical error which the trial court was entitled to fix.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed. The case was remanded so that the judgment could be filed under the substantive case numbers rather than the habitual felon case number and for resentencing in accordance with Blakely.

 

584 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Verrier


NO. COA04-601


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


173 N.C. App. 123; 617 S.E.2d 675; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 1899


January 12, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
September 6, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Forsyth County. Nos. 02 CRS 61455, 03 CRS 4975, 03 CRS 19609, 03 CRS 51347.



DISPOSITION: No error at trial; remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted for taking indecent liberties with a child, being an habitual felon, three counts of third-degree sexual exploitation of a minor, and failure to register as a sex offender. The Forsyth County Superior Court (North Carolina) sentenced him to a total of 120 to 153 months' imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Contrary to defendant's contention, there was substantial evidence of taking indecent liberties with a child. Among other things, the victim testified that defendant tickled her in her privates, that he was tickling her leg and would start going up to her privates. Defendant's arguments that the trial court erred in allowing the introduction of prejudicial evidence and denying his motion for a mistrial both failed under the plain error standard as defendant provided no explanation for why the evidentiary issue was prejudicial and plain error review did not apply to decisions made at the trial judge's discretion, such as the granting of a mistrial. Defendant next argued that his rights to due process and effective assistance of appellate counsel were violated by the failure to his trial counsel to request that the jury selection, bench conferences, and opening and closing statements be recorded. The appellate court found no error, noting that defendant made no motion for such recording. Finally, as to defendant's motion for appropriate relief, the appellate court found that, inter alia, the trial court erroneously aggravated defendant's sentence based on facts not found by a jury.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed. Defendant's motion for appropriate relief was dismissed as to the portion concerning his failure to register as a sex offender. The case was remanded for resentencing.

Property Rights Advocacy Group v. Town of Long Beach


NO. COA04-1374


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


173 N.C. App. 180; 617 S.E.2d 715; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 1924


June 14, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
September 6, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Appeal dismissed by Property Rights Advocacy Group v. Town of Long Beach, 360 N.C. 177, 626 S.E.2d 649, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 1263 (2005)
Motion granted by Advocacy Group v. Town of Long Beach, 627 S.E.2d 464, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1483 (N.C., 2006)
Affirmed by Property Rights Advocacy Group v. Town of Long Beach, 360 N.C. 474, 628 S.E.2d 768, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 41 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Brunswick County. No. 02 CVS 1249.
Property Rights Advocacy Group v. Town of Long Beach, 2004 N.C. App. LEXIS 318 (N.C. Ct. App., Mar. 2, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Brunswick County (North Carolina) court denied the motion for a permanent injunction of plaintiffs, an advocacy group and an individual, declaring both 1998 N.C. Sess. Laws 83 (the Long Beach Act) and a local ordinance (first ordinance) to be constitutional, and awarded costs to defendants, a town and the state. Plaintiffs timely appealed from this order. Defendants sought dismissal of plaintiffs' appeal.


OVERVIEW: In 1998 the general assembly enacted the Long Beach Act, authorizing the town to pass ordinances providing for development of parks on municipal streets. Thereafter, the town enacted the first ordinance, designating as "public parks" all street ends that dead-ended into waterways in the town. The trial court then entered an order declaring that neither the Long Beach Act nor the first ordinance violated the state constitution. The town later repealed the first ordinance, replacing it with a second ordinance that did not close any streets or create street-end public parks. The parties agreed that the first ordinance was no longer before the court. Defendants argued that the relief sought by plaintiffs, a declaration that the first ordinance was unconstitutional, could not be granted in a declaratory judgment action where the ordinance no longer existed. The appeals court concluded that issues pertaining to the first ordinance were no longer before it, and the constitutionality of the Long Beach Act was not before it because there was no justiciable case or controversy concerning the Long Beach Act. Finally, the trial court's award of costs was not preserved for appellate review.


OUTCOME: Plaintiffs' appeal was dismissed.

587 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Carolinas Med. Ctr. v. Emplrs & Carriers Listed in Exhibit A


NO. COA04-707


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


172 N.C. App. 549; 616 S.E.2d 588; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 1773


January 12, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
August 16, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] N.C. Industrial Commission. DRG Cases.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs hospitals sued defendants employers and insurers in the North Carolina Industrial Commission for refusing to pay amounts the Commission approved to the hospitals. The Commission declared N.C. Gen. Stat. § 97-26(b) (1994), as it existed from July 1, 1995 to April 1, 1996, unconstitutional, and found the hospitals were not entitled to the amounts they sought. The hospitals appealed and defendants purported to cross-appeal.


OVERVIEW: Under the Workers' Compensation Act, N.C. Gen. Stat. § 97-1 et seq., diagnostic related grouping (DRG) rates for conditions hospitals treated were set and hospitals were paid more or less than them. Defendants would not pay more than the rates. The Industrial Commission found N.C. Gen. Stat. § 97-26(b) (1994), under which reimbursement amounts were approved, unconstitutional. The appellate court held the Commission could not declare a statute unconstitutional. The appellate court could not consider the question as no certiorari petition was filed, under N.C. R. App. P. 21, nor did a party seek suspension of the Rules of Appellate Procedure, under N.C. R. App. P. 2, nor did the Commission certify the question to the appellate court, under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 97-86 (2004). N.C. R. App. P. 2 should not be used to confer jurisdiction on the appellate court absent a certification from the Industrial Commission. N.C. Gen. Stat. chs. 97 and 135 authorized requiring defendants to pay the approved amounts, so defendants were not entitled to relief under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 135-40.7(8) (1996), barring payments a payor was not legally obligated to pay.


OUTCOME: The lower tribunal's order was vacated.

 

588 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wissink


NO. COA04-1081


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


172 N.C. App. 829; 617 S.E.2d 319; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 1776


May 11, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
August 16, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Stay granted by State v. Wissink, 360 N.C. 77, 620 S.E.2d 527, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 943 (2005)
Review granted by, Stay granted by State v. Wissink, 361 N.C. 180, 640 S.E.2d 392, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1375 (2006)
Reversed by, in part, Remanded by State v. Wissink, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 591 (N.C., June 28, 2007)



DISPOSITION: No error; remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court, Cumberland County (North Carolina), of first degree murder, discharging a firearm into occupied property, and misdemeanor larceny of a motor vehicle, and was sentenced to life imprisonment without parole for first degree murder, 37 to 54 months for discharging a firearm into occupied property, and 60 days for misdemeanor larceny of a motor vehicle. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's accomplice shot a victim in an attempted robbery. The appellate court held a short form murder indictment was not unconstitutional as sentencing enhancement factors did not have to be stated in an indictment. Blakely did not bar amending the alleged crime date at trial as the indictment did not have to state sentence enhancers. The indictment's allegation of a crime date other than that proved, did not require dismissal as the indictment was properly amended, and the State could prove a crime charged was committed on a date other than that in the indictment. The fact that defendant committed a crime on probation did not have to be stated in an indictment, but it was error to add a point to his prior record level when whether he was on probation when he committed the crime was not submitted to a jury and proved beyond a reasonable doubt. His probation did not have the safeguards of a jury trial and proof beyond a reasonable doubt. At sentencing, neither Blakely nor Allen were decided, so he did not knowingly and intelligently admit he was on probation when he committed the crime, as he did not know he had the right to have a jury decide this sentence enhancer.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed, but the matter was remanded for resentencing.

Payne v. Charlotte Heating & Air Conditioning


NO. COA03-1651


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


172 N.C. App. 496; 616 S.E.2d 356; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 1782


October 12, 2004, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
August 16, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion dismissed by Payne v. Charlotte Heating & Air, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 420 (N.C., May 4, 2006)
Motion dismissed by, Moot Payne v. Charlotte Heating & Air Conditioning, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 430 (N.C., May 4, 2006)
Motion granted by Payne v. Charlotte Heating & Air, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 444 (N.C., May 4, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] North Carolina Industrial Commission. I.C. No. 610609.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, an employer and its insurer, sought review of an opinion and an award from the North Carolina Industrial Commission (NCIC), which granted total disability benefits (TDBs) and death benefits (DBs) pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 97-39 (2003) to plaintiff, a deceased employee's estate administratrix. The trial court found that the decedent was last injuriously exposed to asbestosis hazards while employed by the employer.


OVERVIEW: The employee was exposed to asbestos products while working for a prior employer. Thereafter, he had other employment positions before working for the instant employer, wherein he was again exposed to asbestos. Jobs after that employment relationship terminated did not involve any exposure. The employee was eventually diagnosed with pulmonary abnormalities caused by asbestosis. The NCIC reversed the deputy commissioner's decision on the employee's benefits application. It found that the deceased employee had asbestosis, which caused his total disability and significantly contributed to his death, that his last injurious exposure was with the employer, and that he was entitled to TDBs and DBs under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 97-39. On appeal, the court found that the NCIC had authority to decide the death benefits claims. Further, the court held that N.C. Gen. Stat. § 97-61.6 (2003) was unconstitutional, as it violated the Equal Protection Clause. Accordingly, there was no time limitations bar thereunder, and the death benefits claim was deemed timely. There was competent evidence to support the NCIC's findings on the merits of the benefits claim, pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 97-57 (2003).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the opinion and the award of the NCIC.

State v. Dorton


NO. COA04-572


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


172 N.C. App. 759; 617 S.E.2d 97; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 1794


February 16, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
August 16, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Dorton, 360 N.C. 69, 623 S.E.2d 775, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 1168 (2005)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by State v. Dorton, 2007 N.C. App. LEXIS 472 (N.C. Ct. App., Mar. 6, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Scotland County. No. 02 CRS 52068.



DISPOSITION: No error in part, remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Scotland County Superior Court (North Carolina), which convicted him of a second-degree sexual offense and imposed a sentence of imprisonment in the aggravated range.


OVERVIEW: Defendant demanded that the victim, his 16-year-old daughter, engage in oral sex with him. When she refused, he sexually and physically abused her. Defendant's motion for dismissal due to denial of a speedy trial was denied. After a jury trial, defendant was found guilty of a sexual offense and not guilty of second-degree rape. He was sentenced and he appealed. The court found that denial of the dismissal motion was proper, as defendant's speedy trial rights under U.S. Const. amend. VI and N.C. Const. art. I, § 18 were not violated where he was granted multiple continuances and there was no showing of neglect or willfulness by the State. The trial court did not act arbitrarily in denying sequestration of the victim's mother. Denial of defendant's right to inquire into the victim's previous sexual activity for the purpose of attacking her credibility was proper. Other evidentiary rulings concerning admission of a letter, testimony of the victim's state of mind, and disclosure by the State of defendant's statement, were proper. Denial of dismissal was proper, as the evidence was sufficient. However, reversal per se of sentencing was required due to a Blakely violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court with respect to defendant's conviction, but it remanded the matter for resentencing.

State v. Whiteley


NO. COA04-636


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


172 N.C. App. 772; 616 S.E.2d 576; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 1795


February 16, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
August 16, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Ashe County. No. 02CRS1081.



DISPOSITION: Vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Ashe County Superior Court (North Carolina) of having committed a crime against nature. Defendant contended the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss and in submitting the offense of a crime against nature to the jury, on the grounds that the statute creating the offense, N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-177 (2003), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant left a party with the 18-year-old victim and went back to his apartment. The victim had no recollection of leaving the party or any of the events that followed until the next morning. The victim awoke, naked, alone in defendant's bedroom, and had a sharp pain in her swollen vaginal area. The victim's pelvic area was bruised, and her vagina was swollen, red, and bleeding. Something had been forcibly inserted into her vagina, possibly repeatedly. A toxicology screen showed no alcohol, but revealed benzodiazepine. The jury found defendant not guilty of second-degree rape and second-degree sexual offense. The appellate court held that § 14-177 could be used to prosecute conduct involving a minor, conduct involving non-consensual or coercive sexual acts, conduct occurring in a public place, or conduct involving prostitution or solicitation. Thus, the statute was facially constitutional. However, the jury, by its verdict, found that the evidence did not show beyond a reasonable doubt that the act was non-consensual, that is, that defendant was helpless and therefore unable to consent to the sexual act. Thus, § 14-177 was unconstitutionally applied to defendant.


OUTCOME: The conviction was vacated.

State v. Everette


NO. COA03-858


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


172 N.C. App. 237; 616 S.E.2d 237; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 1437


April 21, 2004, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
August 2, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Stay granted by State v. Everette, 620 S.E.2d 199, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 1399 (N.C., 2005)
Stay granted by State v. Everette, 360 N.C. 69, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 1394 (2005)
Review granted by State v. Everette, 361 N.C. 173, 640 S.E.2d 388, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1373 (2006)
Review granted by, Stay granted by State v. Everette, 361 N.C. 173, 640 S.E.2d 388, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1378 (2006)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by State v. Everette, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 1107 (N.C., Nov. 9, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Pitt County. Nos. 01 CRS 063740-41, 02 CRS 012108.



DISPOSITION: No error; remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of two counts of assault with a deadly weapon inflicting serious injury, assault with a firearm on a law enforcement officer, and discharging a firearm into occupied property. The Superior Court, Pitt County (North Carolina), sentenced defendant to a minimum term of 36 months and a maximum term of 53 months in prison for each of the three charges, the terms to run consecutively. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Contrary to defendant's argument, the appellate court found substantial evidence from which a jury could have found that defendant had reasonable grounds to believe that the restaurant was occupied when he fired the shots in its direction. Prior to the subject incident, the restaurant had stayed open until 3:00 a.m., and the restaurant was located in an area where other establishments were open until the early morning hours. As to his sentence, defendant argued that the trial court erred in its finding of four aggravating factors when defendant did not admit to them and a jury did not determine them. The appellate court found that the trial court unilaterally found each of the aggravating factors without submitting them to a jury, thus violating Blakely and defendant's Sixth Amendment right to a jury trial and requiring resentencing. Finally, the appellate court noted that the trial court did not err in finding that each aggravating factor alone outweighed the mitigating factor, a determination it made to provide guidance on remand.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed. The case was remanded for resentencing.

McGladrey & Pullen, LLP v. N.C. State Bd. of CPA Exam'rs


NO. COA04-911


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


171 N.C. App. 610; 615 S.E.2d 339; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 1274


April 12, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
July 19, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review denied by, Notice of appeal dismissed by McGladrey & Pullen, L.L.P v. N.C. State Bd. of CPA Exam'rs, 360 N.C. 65, 621 S.E.2d 627, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 1019 (2005)
Motion granted by McGladrey & Pullen v. Bd. of CPA Ex., 623 S.E.2d 268, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 1400 (N.C., 2005)
Motion granted by McGladrey & Pullen v. Bd. of CPA Ex, 625 S.E.2d 112, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 1202 (N.C., 2005)
Motion granted by McGladrey & Pullen v. Bd. of CPA Ex, 627 S.E.2d 219, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 1338 (N.C., 2005)
Motion granted by McGladrey & Pullen v. Bd. of CPA Ex, 629 S.E.2d 610, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 565 (N.C., 2006)
Affirmed by McGladrey & Pullen, LLP v. N.C. State Bd. of CPA Exam'rs, 360 N.C. 399, 627 S.E.2d 461, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 34 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Wake County. No. 03 CVS 7412.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee North Carolina State Board of Certified Public Accountant Examiners adopted a declaratory ruling that denied, pursuant to N.C. Admin. Code. tit. 21, r. 8N.0307 (2004), appellant certified public accounting firm's request for a proposed name change. The accounting firm petitioned the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina) for judicial review. The superior court affirmed the decision. The accounting firm appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Board determined that the accounting firm's proposed name change from "McGladrey & Pullen, LLP" to "RSM McGladrey & Pullen, LLP, Certified Public Accountants" violated N.C. Admin. Code. tit. 21, r. 8N.0307 as the proposed name had a capacity or tendency to deceive. On appeal, the court found that the Board possessed the authority to regulate certified public accounting (CPA) firms and CPA firm names, N.C. Gen. Stat. § 93-12 (2003). Further, the Board promulgated N.C. Admin. Code tit. 21, r. 8N.0307 to regulate the names of CPA firms. Additionally, the State of North Carolina, through the Board, could regulate deceptive commercial speech without violating the accounting firm's right to freedom of speech under U.S. Const. amend. I. Moreover, the accounting firm failed to present any evidence that the Board treated another company similarly situated to the accounting firm differently or provided preferential treatment in violation of the accounting firm's equal protection rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV. Finally, the trial court's findings of fact and conclusions of law were supported by substantial evidence in the whole record and were not arbitrary or capricious.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

594 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Tutt


NO. COA04-821


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


171 N.C. App. 518; 615 S.E.2d 688; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 1313


March 8, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
July 19, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Guilford County. No. 02 CRS 103990, 03 CRS 024188.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Superior Court, Guilford County (North Carolina), convicted defendant of robbery with a dangerous weapon and conspiracy. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The charges arose out of a store robbery. A photo lineup was admitted at trial without objection. Defendant argued on appeal that the denial of his motion to suppress the lineup identification was error. The appellate court held that the motion to suppress was insufficient to preserve the issue because defendant did not object when the lineup was offered into evidence. While N.C. Gen. Stat. § 8C-1, N.C. R. Evid. 103(a)(2) (2004) permitted appellate review of an evidentiary ruling even though the party failed to object at trial, because N.C. Gen. Stat. § 8C-1, N.C. R. Evid. 103(a)(2) (2004) was inconsistent with N.C. R. App. P. 10(b)(1), the statute failed. Regardless of the title and placement of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 8C-1, N.C. R. Evid. 103 by the general assembly, the text of the rule made it one of practice and procedure. However, because it would have been a manifest injustice to defendant to not review his appeal on the merits after he relied on a procedural statute that was presumed constitutional at the time of trial, the appellate court reviewed the evidence. The trial court did not err in denying the motion to suppress as the lineup was not impermissibly suggestive.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Duff


NO. COA04-1241


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


171 N.C. App. 662; 615 S.E.2d 373; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 1367


May 19, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
July 19, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Motion denied by State v. Duff, 359 N.C. 854, 618 S.E.2d 736, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 816 (N.C., Aug. 9, 2005)
Review denied by, Petition denied by State v. Duff, 359 N.C. 854, 619 S.E.2d 853, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 917 (N.C., Aug. 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Buncombe County. Nos. 03 CRS 13111, 03 CRS 13113, 03 CRS 13115, 03 CRS 57785-86.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded in part; vacated in part; no error in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Buncombe County Court (North Carolina), which convicted him of robbery with a dangerous weapon.


OVERVIEW: The evidence at trial showed that defendant followed the victim into an elevator at a hotel and then followed her to her hotel room where he pushed her inside and robbed her. He then attacked her by pounding her head against a wall until she lost consciousness. When police contacted defendant, he confessed to taking money from the victim. At trial, he sought unsuccessfully to suppress his custodial statement to police. He was convicted. On appeal, the court found that the trial court's finding of fact that defendant was not coerced into a confession due to threats made against his wife was supported by competent evidence because both police officers testified that at no point did they indicate to defendant that his wife would be charged if he did not confess, nor did they promise defendant anything if he offered a confession. The court reversed the conviction of robbery with a dangerous weapon, finding that hands, fists, and feet could not be considered dangerous weapons for the purposes of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-87. Furthermore, the court found that there was no indication that the victim's life was threatened or endangered by an "armed" individual.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for robbery with a dangerous weapon, and remanded the case for entry of judgment on the offense of common law robbery.

Clark v. Foust-Graham


NO. COA04-1266


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


171 N.C. App. 707; 615 S.E.2d 398; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 1365


March 24, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
July 19, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied, Writ denied by, Sub nomine at Goodwin v. Smith, 362 N.C. 680, 670 S.E.2d 563, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 1038 (2008)
Motion denied by Goodwin v. Smith, 362 N.C. 680, 670 S.E.2d 563, 2008 N.C. LEXIS 1065 (2008)
Motion denied by Goodwin v. Smith, 2015 N.C. LEXIS 1119 (N.C., Nov. 5, 2015)
Motion dismissed by Goodwin v. Smith, 2015 N.C. LEXIS 1122 (N.C., Nov. 5, 2015)
Motion granted by Goodwin v. Smith, 2015 N.C. LEXIS 1123 (N.C., Nov. 5, 2015)
Motion dismissed by Goodwin v. Smith, 2015 N.C. LEXIS 1124 (N.C., Nov. 5, 2015)
Motion dismissed by Goodwin v. Smith, 2015 N.C. LEXIS 1128 (N.C., Nov. 5, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Guilford County. No. 03 CVD 6867.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action initially brought on behalf of plaintiff executrix's decedent against defendant wife, a jury in the Guilford County District Court (North Carolina) found that the wife had procured her marriage to the decedent by means of undue influence. The wife appealed.


OVERVIEW: The wife argued that the annulment action could not have been properly maintained by the executrix after the decedent's death. The executrix had filed the case on the decedent's behalf as his guardian ad litem while the decedent was alive. Given that and the fact that substantial property rights hinged on the validity of the marriage, the appellate court ruled that the action did not abate on the decedent's death and that the executrix was entitled to pursue it. Undue influence was a proper ground to annul a marriage. The decedent was elderly at the time of the marriage, and there was evidence, inter alia, that he suffered from dementia and/or Alzheimer's. He was subject to constant association with, and supervision by, the wife and had little association with his family or friends in the months immediately before the marriage. The marriage left the decedent's existing estate plan in doubt and put the wife in a position to substantially reduce the amount that the decedent's daughter would inherit. There was also evidence that the wife procured the marriage and that the decedent was confused at the time of the marriage. Sufficient evidence supported the verdict.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

599 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Curmon


NO. COA04-1480


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


171 N.C. App. 697; 615 S.E.2d 417; 2005 N.C. App. LEXIS 1362


June 9, 2005, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
July 19, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Wake County. No. 03 CRS 28451, 03 CRS 32935.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR AS TO TRIAL; REMANDED FOR STRIKING OF RESTITUTION PROVISION IN THE JUDGMENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina) convicted defendant of first-degree arson after the trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss. Defendant appealed the conviction.


OVERVIEW: In the incident in question, someone drenched a doormat in gasoline, set the mat on fire, and pushed it under a victim's door. In his first argument on appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss because there was insufficient evidence that defendant was the perpetrator. The evidence showed that defendant began to harass the victims, his girlfriend and her new boyfriend. Defendant left a message threatening to burn up the couple if the ex-girlfriend did not return his call. On the night of the fire, defendant left another threatening message. Defendant's cellular telephone records established that he was in the vicinity of the victim's apartment. The gasoline on the doormat indicated that the fire was set deliberately. The appellate court held that this evidence was sufficient to submit the charge of first-degree arson to the jury. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred in ordering him to pay restitution to the victim's new boyfriend for damages suffered as a result of the fire. The State conceded that the trial court's order was not supported by the evidence and had to be vacated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, but the case was remanded for modification of the restitution order.
